"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint:\n\n1. **Original price of each pack of DVDs**: 76 dollars\n2. **Discount on each pack**: 25 dollars\n\nNow, we need to calculate the price you have to pay for each pack after the discount is applied:\n\n3. **Calculate the discounted price**:\n   - Subtract the discount from the original price:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Discounted Price} = \\text{Original Price} - \\text{Discount}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Discounted Price} = 76 \\text{ dollars} - 25 \\text{ dollars} = 51 \\text{ dollars}\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, you have to pay **51 dollars** for each pack of DVDs after the discount is applied."
"To solve the problem of determining how much the candy bar cost, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and question information:\n\n1. **Initial Amount**: Dan had $4 initially.\n2. **Remaining Amount**: After buying the candy bar, Dan was left with $3.\n3. **Cost of the Candy Bar**: The cost of the candy bar is the difference between the initial amount and the remaining amount.\n\nNow, let's calculate the cost of the candy bar step by step:\n\n- **Step 1**: Identify the initial amount of money Dan had.\n  - Initial amount = $4\n\n- **Step 2**: Identify the amount of money Dan had left after buying the candy bar.\n  - Remaining amount = $3\n\n- **Step 3**: Calculate the cost of the candy bar by finding the difference between the initial amount and the remaining amount.\n  - Cost of the candy bar = Initial amount - Remaining amount\n  - Cost of the candy bar = $4 - $3\n\n- **Step 4**: Perform the subtraction to find the cost.\n  - Cost of the candy bar = $1\n\nTherefore, the candy bar cost $1."

"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial number of children on the bus:**  \n   There were initially 28 children on the bus.\n\n2. **Children getting on the bus at the stop:**  \n   At the bus stop, 82 children got on the bus.\n\n3. **Children on the bus after some got off:**  \n   After some children got off, there were 30 children left on the bus.\n\nNow, let's calculate the number of children who got off the bus:\n\n- **Total children on the bus after getting on:**  \n  Initially, there were 28 children, and 82 more got on, so the total number of children on the bus before any got off is:  \n  \\(28 + 82 = 110\\)\n\n- **Children remaining on the bus after some got off:**  \n  After some children got off, there were 30 children left on the bus.\n\n- **Number of children who got off the bus:**  \n  To find out how many children got off, subtract the number of children remaining from the total before any got off:  \n  \\(110 - 30 = 80\\)\n\nFinally, we need to find out how many more children got on the bus than those that got off:\n\n- **Children who got on the bus:** 82\n- **Children who got off the bus:** 80\n\n- **Difference (more children got on than got off):**  \n  \\(82 - 80 = 2\\)\n\nTherefore, 2 more children got on the bus than those that got off."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Initial Amount in Wallet:**\n   - Olivia initially had $3 in her wallet.\n\n2. **Amount Collected from ATM:**\n   - She collected $49 more dollars from an ATM.\n\n3. **Total Amount After ATM Withdrawal:**\n   - Total amount = Initial amount + Amount collected from ATM\n   - Total amount = $3 + $49 = $52\n\n4. **Amount Left After Supermarket Visit:**\n   - After visiting the supermarket, Olivia had $49 left.\n\n5. **Amount Spent at the Supermarket:**\n   - Amount spent = Total amount after ATM withdrawal - Amount left after supermarket visit\n   - Amount spent = $52 - $49 = $3\n\n6. **Difference Between Amount Collected and Amount Spent:**\n   - Difference = Amount collected from ATM - Amount spent at the supermarket\n   - Difference = $49 - $3 = $46\n\nTherefore, Olivia collected $46 more from the ATM than she spent at the supermarket."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Jerry initially had some action figures on his shelf.\n   - He added 7 more action figures to the shelf.\n   - After adding, there are a total of 10 action figures on the shelf.\n\n2. **Identify What We Need to Find:**\n   - We need to find out how many action figures Jerry had initially before adding the 7 more.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of action figures Jerry had initially.\n   - According to the problem, after adding 7 more action figures, the total becomes 10.\n   - This can be expressed as an equation: \n     \\[\n     x + 7 = 10\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( x \\), subtract 7 from both sides of the equation:\n     \\[\n     x + 7 - 7 = 10 - 7\n     \\]\n   - Simplifying gives:\n     \\[\n     x = 3\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Jerry initially had 3 action figures on the shelf.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Jerry had 3 action figures initially on the shelf before adding the 7 more."

This can be expressed as:\n     \\[\n     x - 9 = 12\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( x \\), add 9 to both sides of the equation:\n     \\[\n     x - 9 + 9 = 12 + 9\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     x = 21\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The waiter initially had 21 customers.\n\nTherefore, the waiter had 21 customers at the start."

Therefore, we can write the equation:\n     \\[\n     692 = B + 458\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the equation for \\( B \\):**\n   - Subtract 458 from both sides to find the number of boys:\n     \\[\n     B = 692 - 458\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the result:\n     \\[\n     B = 234\n     \\]\n\n5. **Calculate the total number of pupils:**\n   - The total number of pupils is the sum of the number of girls and boys:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total pupils} = \\text{Number of girls} + \\text{Number of boys}\n     \\]\n   - Substitute the known values:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total pupils} = 692 + 234\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the result:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total pupils} = 926\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, there are 926 pupils in the school."

"To solve the problem, let's break down the information given and follow the steps to find the total number of visitors to Buckingham Palace within 25 days.\n\n### Information Given:\n1. Rachel learned that 703 visitors came to Buckingham Palace on the previous day.\n2. There were 246 visitors on the day they visited.\n\n### Steps to Solve:\n1. **Identify the Days with Known Visitor Counts:**\n   - Day 1 (the day they visited): 246 visitors\n   - Day 2 (the previous day): 703 visitors\n\n2. **Calculate the Total Number of Visitors for the Two Known Days:**\n   - Total visitors for Day 1 and Day 2 = 246 (Day 1) + 703 (Day 2) = 949 visitors\n\n3. **Assume the Average or Estimate for the Remaining Days:**\n   - Since we only have specific data for 2 days, we need to make an assumption or estimate for the remaining 23 days.\n   - Without additional information, we cannot accurately determine the number of visitors for the remaining days. However, if we assume the average number of visitors per day is similar to the known days, we can estimate.\n\n4. **Estimate the Average Number of Visitors:**\n   - Average visitors for the 2 known days = (246 + 703) / 2 = 474.5 visitors per day\n\n5. **Estimate the Total Number of Visitors for 25 Days:**\n   - Total estimated visitors for 25 days = 474.5 visitors/day * 25 days = 11,862.5 visitors\n\n6. **Round to the Nearest Whole Number:**\n   - Since the number of visitors must be a whole number, round 11,862.5 to 11,863 visitors.\n\n### Conclusion:\nBased on the assumption that the average number of visitors per day is similar to the two known days, approximately 11,863 visitors visited Buckingham Palace within 25 days."

'To solve the problem of determining how many oranges are in each group when 356 oranges are organized into 178 groups, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the Total Number of Oranges:**\n   - Total number of oranges = 356\n\n2. **Identify the Number of Groups:**\n   - Number of groups of oranges = 178\n\n3. **Determine the Number of Oranges per Group:**\n   - To find out how many oranges are in each group, divide the total number of oranges by the number of groups.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Oranges per group} = \\frac{\\text{Total number of oranges}}{\\text{Number of groups}} = \\frac{356}{178}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the Division:**\n   - Calculate \\( \\frac{356}{178} \\).\n\n   \\[\n   \\frac{356}{178} = 2\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - There are 2 oranges in each group.\n\nTherefore, each group contains 2 oranges.'

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - The machine made 8 shirts today.\n   - The machine can make 2 shirts per minute.\n\n2. **Determine the Number of Minutes Worked:**\n   - Since the machine makes 2 shirts per minute, we need to find out how many minutes it takes to make 8 shirts.\n\n3. **Calculate the Time:**\n   - To find the number of minutes the machine worked, divide the total number of shirts made today by the number of shirts the machine can make per minute.\n   - Calculation: \\( \\frac{8 \\text{ shirts}}{2 \\text{ shirts per minute}} = 4 \\text{ minutes} \\).\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - The machine worked for 4 minutes today to make 8 shirts.\n\nTherefore, the machine worked for 4 minutes today."
'To solve the problem of dividing 15 eggs into 3 groups, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the Total Number of Eggs:**\n   - Rebecca has a total of 15 eggs.\n\n2. **Determine the Number of Groups:**\n   - Rebecca wants to split the eggs into 3 groups.\n\n3. **Calculate the Number of Eggs per Group:**\n   - To find out how many eggs each group will have, divide the total number of eggs by the number of groups.\n   - Calculation: \\( \\frac{15 \\text{ eggs}}{3 \\text{ groups}} = 5 \\text{ eggs per group} \\).\n\n4. **Verify the Calculation:**\n   - Multiply the number of eggs per group by the number of groups to ensure it equals the total number of eggs: \n   - \\( 5 \\text{ eggs/group} \\times 3 \\text{ groups} = 15 \\text{ eggs} \\).\n\nTherefore, each group will have 5 eggs.'
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Matthew gave crackers to his friends.\n   - He gave 2 crackers to each friend.\n   - He has 11 friends.\n\n2. **Calculate the Total Number of Crackers Given:**\n   - Since Matthew gave 2 crackers to each of his 11 friends, we need to calculate the total number of crackers he gave away.\n   - Total crackers given = Number of friends × Crackers per friend\n   - Total crackers given = 11 friends × 2 crackers/friend = 22 crackers\n\n3. **Determine How Many Crackers Matthew Had Initially:**\n   - Since the problem states that Matthew gave these crackers to his friends, the total number of crackers he had initially is the same as the total number he gave away.\n\nTherefore, Matthew initially had 22 crackers."
'To solve the problem of determining how much money Olivia had initially, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Olivia spent 78 dollars at a supermarket.\n   - Olivia has 33 dollars left with her.\n\n2. **Define the Problem:**\n   - We need to find out how much money Olivia had initially before spending any money.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the amount of money Olivia had initially.\n   - After spending 78 dollars, she has 33 dollars left.\n   - Therefore, the equation can be set up as:\n     \\[\n     x - 78 = 33\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( x \\), add 78 to both sides of the equation:\n     \\[\n     x - 78 + 78 = 33 + 78\n     \\]\n   - Simplifying the equation gives:\n     \\[\n     x = 111\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Olivia initially had 111 dollars.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Olivia had 111 dollars initially.'
"To solve this problem, we need to calculate how much money Lewis earns in total over 73 harvest seasons, given that he earns $1,357 every week and each harvest season lasts for 223 weeks. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Weekly Earnings:**\n   - Lewis earns $1,357 every week.\n\n2. **Weeks per Harvest Season:**\n   - Each harvest season lasts for 223 weeks.\n\n3. **Earnings per Harvest Season:**\n   - To find out how much Lewis earns in one harvest season, multiply his weekly earnings by the number of weeks in a season:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Earnings per season} = 1,357 \\times 223\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate Earnings per Harvest Season:**\n   \\[\n   1,357 \\times 223 = 302,611\n   \\]\n   So, Lewis earns $302,611 in one harvest season.\n\n5. **Number of Harvest Seasons:**\n   - Lewis works for 73 harvest seasons.\n\n6. **Total Earnings Over 73 Harvest Seasons:**\n   - To find the total earnings over 73 seasons, multiply the earnings per season by the number of seasons:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total earnings} = 302,611 \\times 73\n   \\]\n\n7. **Calculate Total Earnings:**\n   \\[\n   302,611 \\times 73 = 22,070,603\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, Lewis will earn a total of $22,070,603 over 73 harvest seasons."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Total number of students surveyed:** 310 students\n2. **Number of students who suggested adding mashed potatoes:** 185 students\n3. **Number of students who suggested adding bacon:** This is the remaining number of students after accounting for those who suggested mashed potatoes.\n\nTo find the number of students who suggested adding bacon, we need to subtract the number of students who suggested mashed potatoes from the total number of students surveyed:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Number of students who suggested bacon} = \\text{Total number of students} - \\text{Number of students who suggested mashed potatoes}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\text{Number of students who suggested bacon} = 310 - 185\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\text{Number of students who suggested bacon} = 125\n\\]\n\nTherefore, 125 students suggested adding bacon to the menu."

"To solve this problem, we need to determine the total number of students who suggested adding bacon to the menu. We have two groups of students to consider:\n\n1. Students who suggested adding both mashed potatoes and bacon.\n2. Students who suggested adding only bacon.\n\nLet's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the groups:**\n   - Group A: Students who suggested both mashed potatoes and bacon = 218 students.\n   - Group B: Students who suggested only bacon = 351 students.\n\n2. **Calculate the total number of students who suggested adding bacon:**\n   - The total number of students who suggested adding bacon is the sum of students in Group A and Group B.\n   - Total students suggesting bacon = Students suggesting both mashed potatoes and bacon + Students suggesting only bacon.\n\n3. **Perform the calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total students suggesting bacon} = 218 + 351 = 569\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, 569 students suggested adding bacon to the menu."
'To solve the problem of finding the total number of cookies, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Each bag contains 41 cookies.\n   - There are 53 bags.\n\n2. **Set Up the Calculation:**\n   - To find the total number of cookies, multiply the number of cookies per bag by the number of bags.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total number of cookies} = \\text{Number of cookies per bag} \\times \\text{Number of bags}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total number of cookies} = 41 \\times 53\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate:**\n   - First, multiply 41 by 53:\n     \\[\n     41 \\times 53 = 2173\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The total number of cookies is 2,173.\n\nTherefore, if each bag contains 41 cookies and there are 53 bags, you would have a total of 2,173 cookies.'

"To solve the problem, we need to calculate the total revenue generated from selling the t-shirts during the Arkansas and Texas Tech game. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the profit per t-shirt:**\n   - The Razorback shop makes $215 off each t-shirt.\n\n2. **Identify the number of t-shirts sold:**\n   - They sold 20 t-shirts during the game.\n\n3. **Calculate the total revenue from t-shirts:**\n   - Multiply the number of t-shirts sold by the profit per t-shirt:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total revenue from t-shirts} = \\text{Number of t-shirts sold} \\times \\text{Profit per t-shirt}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total revenue from t-shirts} = 20 \\times 215\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the multiplication:**\n   \\[\n   20 \\times 215 = 4300\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the Razorback shop made $4,300 from selling the t-shirts during the Arkansas and Texas Tech game."
"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Number of Children on the Bus:**\n   - There were initially 36 children on the bus.\n\n2. **Children Getting Off the Bus:**\n   - 68 children got off the bus.\n\n3. **Children on the Bus After Some Got On:**\n   - After some children got on the bus, there were 12 children altogether on the bus.\n\nNow, let's calculate the number of children who got on the bus and how many more children got off than got on:\n\n### Step-by-Step Calculation:\n\n1. **Calculate the Number of Children Remaining After Some Got Off:**\n   - If 68 children got off the bus, the number of children remaining would be:\n     \\[\n     36 - 68 = -32\n     \\]\n   - Since it's not possible to have a negative number of children on the bus, this indicates that more children got on the bus to make the total 12.\n\n2. **Calculate the Number of Children Who Got On the Bus:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of children who got on the bus.\n   - After 68 children got off, the bus would have had \\(-32\\) children, but since this is not possible, we need to add \\( x \\) children to reach 12:\n     \\[\n     -32 + x = 12\n     \\]\n   - Solving for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 12 + 32 = 44\n     \\]\n   - Therefore, 44 children got on the bus.\n\n3. **Calculate How Many More Children Got Off Than Got On:**\n   - The number of children who got off the bus is 68.\n   - The number of children who got on the bus is 44.\n   - The difference is:\n     \\[\n     68 - 44 = 24\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, 24 more children got off the bus than those who got on."
"To solve the problem of how many cookies each guest received, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Total Number of Cookies:**\n   - Total cookies made by Brenda's mother: 14\n\n2. **Understand the Number of Guests:**\n   - Number of guests: 2\n\n3. **Divide the Cookies Equally:**\n   - Since the cookies are divided equally among the guests, we need to divide the total number of cookies by the number of guests.\n\n4. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Divide 14 cookies by 2 guests:  \n     \\[\n     \\frac{14}{2} = 7\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each guest received 7 cookies.\n\nTherefore, each of the 2 guests had 7 cookies."

'To find the cost of each t-shirt, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Total revenue from selling t-shirts: $51\n   - Number of t-shirts sold: 3\n\n2. **Identify What We Need to Find:**\n   - The cost of each individual t-shirt.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the cost of each t-shirt.\n   - Since 3 t-shirts were sold, the total revenue can be expressed as: \n     \\[\n     3x = 51\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Divide both sides of the equation by 3 to find \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{51}{3}\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the division:\n     \\[\n     x = 17\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The cost of each t-shirt is $17.\n\nTherefore, each t-shirt costs $17.'

'To determine how many pages Frank read per day, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the total number of pages in the book.**\n   - The book has a total of 112 pages.\n\n2. **Identify the total number of days it took Frank to finish the book.**\n   - It took Frank 16 days to finish the book.\n\n3. **Calculate the number of pages Frank read per day.**\n   - To find the number of pages read per day, divide the total number of pages by the total number of days.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Pages per day} = \\frac{\\text{Total pages}}{\\text{Total days}} = \\frac{112}{16}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the division.**\n   - \\(\\frac{112}{16} = 7\\)\n\nTherefore, Frank read 7 pages per day.'
"To determine how many books you have already read from the 'crazy silly school' series, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the total number of books in the series:**\n   - Total number of books = 20\n\n2. **Identify the number of books you have yet to read:**\n   - Unread books = 5\n\n3. **Calculate the number of books you have already read:**\n   - Subtract the number of unread books from the total number of books:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Books already read} = \\text{Total number of books} - \\text{Unread books} = 20 - 5\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the calculation:**\n   - Books already read = 15\n\nTherefore, you have already read 15 books from the 'crazy silly school' series."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Balloons:**\n   - Allan initially brought 3 balloons to the park.\n   - Jake brought 5 balloons to the park.\n\n2. **Additional Balloons:**\n   - Allan bought 2 more balloons at the park.\n\n3. **Total Balloons Calculation:**\n   - First, calculate the total number of balloons Allan has after buying more:\n     - Allan's initial balloons: 3\n     - Additional balloons Allan bought: 2\n     - Total balloons Allan has: \\(3 + 2 = 5\\)\n\n4. **Total Balloons for Both:**\n   - Now, add the total number of balloons Allan has to the number of balloons Jake has:\n     - Allan's total balloons: 5\n     - Jake's balloons: 5\n     - Total balloons Allan and Jake have together: \\(5 + 5 = 10\\)\n\nTherefore, Allan and Jake have a total of 10 balloons at the park."
"To solve the problem of how many marbles Josh has now, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Initial Information:**\n   - Josh originally had 19 marbles.\n\n2. **Understand the Change:**\n   - Josh lost 11 marbles.\n\n3. **Calculate the Remaining Marbles:**\n   - Start with the original number of marbles: 19\n   - Subtract the number of marbles lost: 19 - 11\n\n4. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - 19 - 11 = 8\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Josh now has 8 marbles remaining in his collection.\n\nTherefore, after losing 11 marbles, Josh has 8 marbles left."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Balloons:**\n   - Allan initially brought 6 balloons to the park.\n   - Jake initially brought 3 balloons to the park.\n\n2. **Additional Balloons:**\n   - Jake bought 4 more balloons at the park.\n\n3. **Total Balloons:**\n   - Allan's total balloons = 6 (since he didn't buy any more).\n   - Jake's total balloons = 3 (initial) + 4 (additional) = 7.\n\n4. **Comparison:**\n   - To find out how many more balloons Jake had than Allan, subtract the number of balloons Allan had from the number of balloons Jake had:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Difference} = \\text{Jake's total balloons} - \\text{Allan's total balloons} = 7 - 6 = 1\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, Jake had 1 more balloon than Allan in the park."
'To solve the problem of determining how many pencils Faye has, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Faye is organizing her pencils into rows.\n   - There are 14 rows.\n   - Each row contains 11 pencils.\n\n2. **List the Information:**\n   - Number of rows = 14\n   - Number of pencils per row = 11\n\n3. **Calculate the Total Number of Pencils:**\n   - To find the total number of pencils, multiply the number of rows by the number of pencils per row.\n   - Total pencils = Number of rows × Number of pencils per row\n   - Total pencils = 14 × 11\n\n4. **Perform the Multiplication:**\n   - 14 × 11 = 154\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Faye has a total of 154 pencils.\n\nTherefore, Faye has 154 pencils.'

"To solve the problem of determining how many apples remained after the chef used some for pies, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Initial Number of Apples**: The chef started with 58 apples.\n\n2. **Apples Used**: The chef used 35 apples to make pies.\n\n3. **Calculation of Remaining Apples**: To find out how many apples are left, subtract the number of apples used from the initial number of apples.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Remaining Apples} = \\text{Initial Apples} - \\text{Apples Used}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Remaining Apples} = 58 - 35\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the Subtraction**:\n\n   \\[\n   58 - 35 = 23\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion**: After using 35 apples, the chef has 23 apples remaining.\n\nTherefore, the number of apples that remained is 23."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - You have 26 bags.\n   - Each bag contains an equal number of cookies.\n   - The total number of cookies is 52.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of cookies in each bag.\n   - Since there are 26 bags, the total number of cookies can be expressed as \\( 26 \\times x \\).\n\n3. **Use the Total Number of Cookies:**\n   - We know the total number of cookies is 52.\n   - Therefore, the equation is: \n     \\[\n     26 \\times x = 52\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve for \\( x \\):**\n   - Divide both sides of the equation by 26 to find \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{52}{26}\n     \\]\n\n5. **Calculate:**\n   - Perform the division:\n     \\[\n     x = 2\n     \\]\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each bag contains 2 cookies.\n\nTherefore, each bag has 2 cookies."

"To solve the problem, we need to determine how many pots are required if each pot contains 40 flowers and there are 400 flowers in total. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Each pot contains 40 flowers.\n   - There are 400 flowers in total.\n\n2. **Set Up the Calculation:**\n   - We need to find out how many pots are needed to hold all 400 flowers.\n   - Since each pot holds 40 flowers, we can use division to find the number of pots.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Divide the total number of flowers by the number of flowers per pot:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Number of pots} = \\frac{\\text{Total number of flowers}}{\\text{Number of flowers per pot}} = \\frac{400}{40}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Calculate:**\n   - \\(\\frac{400}{40} = 10\\)\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - There are 10 pots in total.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that there are 10 pots."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Ed had 27 marbles.\n   - Ed had 5 more marbles than Doug.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( D \\) represent the number of marbles Doug initially had.\n   - According to the information, Ed had 5 more marbles than Doug, so we can write the equation:\n     \\[\n     E = D + 5\n     \\]\n   - We know that Ed had 27 marbles, so substitute \\( E \\) with 27:\n     \\[\n     27 = D + 5\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve for \\( D \\):**\n   - Subtract 5 from both sides of the equation to solve for \\( D \\):\n     \\[\n     27 - 5 = D\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     22 = D\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Doug initially had 22 marbles.\n\nTherefore, Doug initially had 22 marbles."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Identify the Variables:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of pages of reading homework Rachel had to complete.\n\n2. **Understand the Relationships:**\n   - Rachel had 4 more pages of math homework than reading homework. This can be expressed as:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Math homework pages} = x + 4\n     \\]\n   - Rachel had to complete a total of 7 pages of math homework.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - From the information above, we know:\n     \\[\n     x + 4 = 7\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Subtract 4 from both sides to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x + 4 - 4 = 7 - 4\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     x = 3\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Rachel had to complete 3 pages of reading homework.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Rachel had to complete 3 pages of reading homework."

Therefore, we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     x + 4 = 8\n     \\]\n\n5. **Solve the equation for \\( x \\):**\n   - Subtract 4 from both sides of the equation to isolate \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 8 - 4\n     \\]\n   - Simplify the right side:\n     \\[\n     x = 4\n     \\]\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - Tiffany had 4 bags of cans on Monday.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Tiffany had 4 bags on Monday."

"To solve this problem, let's break down the information given and follow the steps to find the answer.\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - There are 10 different books in the series.\n   - There are 11 different movies in the series.\n   - You have read 13 books.\n   - You have watched 12 movies.\n\n2. **Analyze the Information:**\n   - The statement that you have read 13 books is incorrect because there are only 10 different books available in the series. Therefore, you can only read a maximum of 10 books.\n   - Similarly, the statement that you have watched 12 movies is incorrect because there are only 11 different movies available in the series. Therefore, you can only watch a maximum of 11 movies.\n\n3. **Correct the Information:**\n   - You have read all 10 books.\n   - You have watched all 11 movies.\n\n4. **Calculate the Difference:**\n   - Number of books read: 10\n   - Number of movies watched: 11\n   - Difference: 10 (books) - 11 (movies) = -1\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - You have read 1 fewer book than the number of movies you have watched.\n\nTherefore, you have read 1 fewer book than movies."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Determine the number of invitations in each package:**\n   - Each package contains 14 invitations.\n\n2. **Calculate the total number of invitations from the packages:**\n   - Carol bought 6 packages.\n   - Total invitations from packages = 14 invitations/package × 6 packages = 84 invitations.\n\n3. **Add the extra invitations Carol bought:**\n   - Carol bought an additional 11 extra invitations.\n\n4. **Calculate the total number of invitations Carol has:**\n   - Total invitations = Invitations from packages + Extra invitations\n   - Total invitations = 84 invitations + 11 invitations = 95 invitations.\n\nTherefore, Carol can invite 95 friends."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Rate of Production:**\n   - The machine can make 3 shirts per minute.\n\n2. **Total Production:**\n   - The machine made a total of 6 shirts.\n\n3. **Determine the Time Required:**\n   - We need to find out how many minutes the machine was working to make 6 shirts.\n\n4. **Calculate the Time:**\n   - Since the machine makes 3 shirts per minute, we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Number of shirts made} = \\text{Rate of production} \\times \\text{Time}\n     \\]\n   - Plug in the known values:\n     \\[\n     6 = 3 \\times \\text{Time}\n     \\]\n\n5. **Solve for Time:**\n   - Divide both sides of the equation by 3 to solve for Time:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Time} = \\frac{6}{3} = 2\n     \\]\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - The machine was working for 2 minutes to make 6 shirts.\n\nTherefore, the machine worked for **2 minutes**."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Information:**\n   - Danny found 63 bottle caps at the park.\n   - Danny threw away 51 old bottle caps.\n   - Danny now has 33 bottle caps in his collection.\n\n2. **Objective:**\n   - Determine how many bottle caps Danny had initially before finding new ones and discarding old ones.\n\n3. **Step-by-Step Calculation:**\n\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of bottle caps Danny had initially.\n   - After finding 63 new bottle caps, Danny's collection increased by 63 caps.\n   - After throwing away 51 old bottle caps, Danny's collection decreased by 51 caps.\n   - The final number of bottle caps Danny has is 33.\n\n   We can set up the equation based on these changes:\n\n   \\[\n   x + 63 - 51 = 33\n   \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n\n   - Simplify the equation:\n     \\[\n     x + 12 = 33\n     \\]\n\n   - Subtract 12 from both sides to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 33 - 12\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     x = 21\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Danny initially had 21 bottle caps in his collection.\n\nTherefore, Danny had 21 bottle caps at first."
"To solve the problem, we need to find the difference in the number of bottles between regular soda and diet soda. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the number of bottles of each type of soda:**\n   - Regular soda: 67 bottles\n   - Diet soda: 9 bottles\n\n2. **Calculate the difference in the number of bottles:**\n   - Subtract the number of diet soda bottles from the number of regular soda bottles:\n     \\[\n     67 - 9 = 58\n     \\]\n\n3. **Conclusion:**\n   - The grocery store has 58 more bottles of regular soda than diet soda.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that the grocery store has 58 more bottles of regular soda than diet soda."

The additional 78 kids from outside the county who attended the camp should not be included in the count of kids from Lawrence County.\n\nLet's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Kids who stayed home**: 644,997\n2. **Kids from Lawrence County who went to camp**: 893,835\n3. **Additional kids from outside the county who attended the camp**: 78 (This number is not relevant for the total count of kids in Lawrence County)\n\nNow, we add the number of kids who stayed home and the number of kids from Lawrence County who went to camp:\n\n\\[ \n644,997 \\text{ (stayed home)} + 893,835 \\text{ (went to camp)} = 1,538,832 \n\\]\n\nTherefore, the total number of kids in Lawrence County is 1,538,832."
'To solve the problem of how many rows Faye can make with 30 pencils, placing 5 pencils in each row, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Total number of pencils: 30\n   - Number of pencils per row: 5\n\n2. **Set Up the Calculation:**\n   - We need to determine how many groups of 5 pencils can be made from a total of 30 pencils.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Divide the total number of pencils by the number of pencils per row:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Number of rows} = \\frac{\\text{Total number of pencils}}{\\text{Number of pencils per row}} = \\frac{30}{5}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Calculate:**\n   - \\(\\frac{30}{5} = 6\\)\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Faye can make 6 rows of pencils if she places 5 pencils in each row.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Faye can make 6 rows.'

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided in the hint:\n\n1. **Initial Number of Crackers:**\n   - Matthew originally had 15 crackers.\n\n2. **Crackers Remaining:**\n   - After giving away some crackers, Matthew had 10 crackers left.\n\n3. **Crackers Given Away:**\n   - The total number of crackers given away is calculated as follows:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Crackers Given Away} = \\text{Initial Crackers} - \\text{Remaining Crackers} = 15 - 10 = 5\n     \\]\n\n4. **Number of Friends:**\n   - Matthew has 5 friends.\n\n5. **Crackers Distributed Equally:**\n   - The 5 crackers were distributed equally among the 5 friends.\n\n6. **Crackers Each Friend Ate:**\n   - To find out how many crackers each friend ate, divide the total crackers given away by the number of friends:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Crackers per Friend} = \\frac{\\text{Crackers Given Away}}{\\text{Number of Friends}} = \\frac{5}{5} = 1\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, each of Matthew's 5 friends ate 1 cracker."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Identify the number of small seats:**\n   - The Ferris wheel has 2 small seats.\n\n2. **Determine the capacity of each small seat:**\n   - Each small seat can hold 14 people.\n\n3. **Calculate the total number of people that can ride on the small seats:**\n   - Multiply the number of small seats by the capacity of each small seat:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total people on small seats} = \\text{Number of small seats} \\times \\text{Capacity of each small seat}\n     \\]\n   - Substitute the given values:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total people on small seats} = 2 \\times 14 = 28\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, a total of 28 people can ride the Ferris wheel on the small seats."
'To determine how many days the 360 soda bottles would last if Debby drinks 9 soda bottles per day, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the total number of soda bottles:**\n   - Debby bought 360 soda bottles.\n\n2. **Determine the daily consumption of soda bottles:**\n   - Debby drinks 9 soda bottles per day.\n\n3. **Calculate the number of days the soda bottles will last:**\n   - To find out how many days the soda bottles will last, divide the total number of soda bottles by the number of soda bottles consumed per day.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of days} = \\frac{\\text{Total soda bottles}}{\\text{Soda bottles per day}} = \\frac{360}{9}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the division:**\n   - \\(\\frac{360}{9} = 40\\)\n\nTherefore, the 360 soda bottles will last for 40 days if Debby drinks 9 soda bottles per day.'
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Identify the number of diet soda bottles:**\n   - The grocery store had 4 bottles of diet soda.\n\n2. **Determine the relationship between diet soda and regular soda:**\n   - The store had 79 more bottles of regular soda than diet soda.\n\n3. **Set up the equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of regular soda bottles.\n   - According to the problem, \\( x = \\text{number of diet soda bottles} + 79 \\).\n\n4. **Substitute the known value:**\n   - We know there are 4 bottles of diet soda, so substitute 4 into the equation:\n   \\[\n   x = 4 + 79\n   \\]\n\n5. **Calculate the number of regular soda bottles:**\n   \\[\n   x = 83\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the grocery store had 83 bottles of regular soda."
"To solve the problem, we need to determine how many t-shirts were sold by the Razorback t-shirt shop. We know the following:\n\n1. Total revenue from selling t-shirts: $60\n2. Profit per t-shirt sold: $10\n\nWe can use these pieces of information to find the number of t-shirts sold. Here's how to solve the problem step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the formula**: \n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of t-shirts sold} = \\frac{\\text{Total revenue}}{\\text{Profit per t-shirt}}\n   \\]\n\n2. **Substitute the known values into the formula**:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of t-shirts sold} = \\frac{60}{10}\n   \\]\n\n3. **Perform the division**:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of t-shirts sold} = 6\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the Razorback t-shirt shop sold 6 t-shirts."
'To find out how many pages are in the book, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Frank reads 22 pages per day.\n   - It took him 569 days to finish the book.\n\n2. **Calculate the Total Number of Pages:**\n   - Since Frank reads 22 pages each day and it took him 569 days to finish the book, we can calculate the total number of pages by multiplying the number of pages he reads per day by the number of days it took him to finish the book.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total pages} = 22 \\, \\text{pages/day} \\times 569 \\, \\text{days}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total pages} = 22 \\times 569 = 12,518\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the book has 12,518 pages.'

This suggests that the number of bird families that flew away includes families from other areas as well, or there is an error in the initial data.\n\n3. **Calculate the Number of Bird Families that Stayed:**\n   - If 45 bird families were living near the mountain initially, and all of them flew away, then 0 bird families stayed behind.\n\n4. **Calculate How Many More Bird Families Flew Away than Stayed:**\n   - Since 0 bird families stayed behind, the number of bird families that flew away (86) is 86 more than those that stayed.\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - 86 more bird families flew away for the winter than those that stayed behind.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that 86 more bird families flew away for the winter than those that stayed behind."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Allan's Balloons:**\n   - Initially, Allan brought 2 balloons to the park.\n   - Then, Allan bought 3 more balloons at the park.\n   - Total balloons Allan has = 2 (initial) + 3 (bought) = 5 balloons.\n\n2. **Jake's Balloons:**\n   - Jake brought 6 balloons to the park.\n   - Total balloons Jake has = 6 balloons.\n\n3. **Comparison:**\n   - We need to find out how many more balloons Jake has than Allan.\n   - Jake's balloons = 6\n   - Allan's balloons = 5\n   - Difference = Jake's balloons - Allan's balloons = 6 - 5 = 1\n\nTherefore, Jake has 1 more balloon than Allan in the park."

We can do this by following these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Shirley sold 25 cases of boxes of trefoils.\n   - Each case contains 14 boxes.\n\n2. **Calculate the Total Number of Boxes:**\n   - To find the total number of boxes, multiply the number of cases by the number of boxes per case.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total number of boxes} = \\text{Number of cases} \\times \\text{Number of boxes per case}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total number of boxes} = 25 \\times 14\n   \\]\n\n3. **Perform the Multiplication:**\n\n   \\[\n   25 \\times 14 = 350\n   \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Shirley needs to deliver a total of 350 boxes of trefoils.\n\nTherefore, the answer is 350 boxes.'

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Total number of pizzas ordered: 7\n   - Total number of slices from all pizzas: 14\n   - Each pizza has the same number of slices.\n\n2. **Determine the Number of Slices per Pizza:**\n   - We need to find out how many slices are in each pizza. Since each pizza has the same number of slices, we can use division to find the answer.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Total slices from all pizzas = 14\n   - Total number of pizzas = 7\n   - To find the number of slices per pizza, divide the total number of slices by the total number of pizzas:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Slices per pizza} = \\frac{\\text{Total slices}}{\\text{Total pizzas}} = \\frac{14}{7} = 2\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each pizza has 2 slices.\n\nTherefore, there are 2 slices in each pizza."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Each pizza has 2 slices.\n   - There are a total of 28 slices.\n\n2. **Define the Problem:**\n   - We need to find out how many pizzas were ordered.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of pizzas ordered.\n   - Since each pizza has 2 slices, the total number of slices from \\( x \\) pizzas is \\( 2x \\).\n\n4. **Use the Given Information:**\n   - We know the total number of slices is 28.\n   - Therefore, we can set up the equation: \n     \\[\n     2x = 28\n     \\]\n\n5. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Divide both sides of the equation by 2 to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{28}{2} = 14\n     \\]\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - The number of pizzas ordered is 14.\n\nTherefore, 14 pizzas were ordered."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Information Given:**\n   - Danny found 30 bottle caps at the park.\n   - Danny found 14 wrappers at the park.\n\n2. **Question:**\n   - How many more bottle caps than wrappers did Danny find at the park?\n\n3. **Steps to Solve:**\n   - First, identify the number of bottle caps Danny found at the park: 30 bottle caps.\n   - Next, identify the number of wrappers Danny found at the park: 14 wrappers.\n   - To find out how many more bottle caps than wrappers Danny found, subtract the number of wrappers from the number of bottle caps.\n\n4. **Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of more bottle caps than wrappers} = \\text{Number of bottle caps} - \\text{Number of wrappers}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   = 30 - 14\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   = 16\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Danny found 16 more bottle caps than wrappers at the park.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Danny found 16 more bottle caps than wrappers at the park."
'To solve the problem of determining how many oranges are harvested per day, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - They harvest 8 sacks of oranges per day.\n   - Each sack contains 35 oranges.\n\n2. **Calculate the Total Number of Oranges Harvested Per Day:**\n   - Multiply the number of sacks by the number of oranges per sack.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total oranges per day} = \\text{Number of sacks per day} \\times \\text{Oranges per sack}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total oranges per day} = 8 \\times 35\n   \\]\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - \\(8 \\times 35 = 280\\)\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - They harvest 280 oranges per day.\n\nTherefore, the answer is 280 oranges per day.'
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the amounts spent:**\n   - Edward spent $16 on books.\n   - Edward spent $8 on pens.\n\n2. **Determine how much more Edward spent on books than on pens:**\n   - To find out how much more he spent on books, subtract the amount spent on pens from the amount spent on books.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Amount more spent on books} = \\text{Amount spent on books} - \\text{Amount spent on pens}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Amount more spent on books} = 16 - 8\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Amount more spent on books} = 8\n   \\]\n\n3. **Conclusion:**\n   - Edward spent $8 more on books than on pens.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Edward spent $8 more on books than on pens."
"To solve the problem of how many necklaces Emily can make, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Requirements:**\n   - Each necklace requires 8 beads.\n\n2. **Determine the Total Beads Available:**\n   - Emily has a total of 16 beads.\n\n3. **Calculate the Number of Necklaces:**\n   - To find out how many necklaces Emily can make, divide the total number of beads by the number of beads required for each necklace.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of necklaces} = \\frac{\\text{Total beads}}{\\text{Beads per necklace}} = \\frac{16}{8} = 2\n   \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Emily can make 2 necklaces with the 16 beads she has.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Emily can make 2 necklaces."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Amount**: Dan initially had $4.\n\n2. **Amount Left After Purchase**: After buying the candy bar, Dan had $3 left.\n\n3. **Calculation of Cost**: To find out how much the candy bar cost, we need to determine how much money Dan spent. This can be calculated by subtracting the amount of money he had left after the purchase from the initial amount he had.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Cost of the candy bar} = \\text{Initial amount} - \\text{Amount left}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Cost of the candy bar} = 4 - 3\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Cost of the candy bar} = 1\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the candy bar cost $1."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Information:**\n   - Rachel picked 2 ripe apples from the tree.\n   - After picking, the tree has 7 apples still on it.\n   - Out of these 7 apples, 6 are ripe.\n\n2. **Determine the Total Number of Ripe Apples Initially:**\n   - Since Rachel picked 2 ripe apples, these were originally on the tree.\n   - After picking, there are still 6 ripe apples on the tree.\n\n3. **Calculate the Initial Number of Ripe Apples:**\n   - The 6 ripe apples still on the tree plus the 2 ripe apples Rachel picked equals the total number of ripe apples the tree had initially.\n   - Therefore, the initial number of ripe apples is \\(6 + 2 = 8\\).\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - The tree initially had 8 ripe apples.\n\nSo, the tree had 8 ripe apples to begin with."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - The machine made 9 shirts yesterday.\n   - The machine can make 3 shirts per minute.\n\n2. **Determine the Time Taken:**\n   - We need to find out how many minutes the machine worked yesterday to make 9 shirts.\n\n3. **Calculate the Time:**\n   - Since the machine makes 3 shirts per minute, we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Time (in minutes)} = \\frac{\\text{Number of shirts made}}{\\text{Shirts per minute}}\n     \\]\n   - Plug in the numbers:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Time (in minutes)} = \\frac{9 \\text{ shirts}}{3 \\text{ shirts per minute}} = 3 \\text{ minutes}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - The machine worked for 3 minutes yesterday to make 9 shirts.\n\nTherefore, the machine worked for **3 minutes** yesterday."

"To solve the problem of determining how much money Edward spent, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and perform the necessary calculations:\n\n1. **Initial Amount**: Edward initially had $13.\n\n2. **Current Amount**: Edward now has $3.\n\n3. **Calculation**: To find out how much money Edward spent, we need to calculate the difference between the initial amount and the current amount.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Amount Spent} = \\text{Initial Amount} - \\text{Current Amount}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Amount Spent} = 13 - 3\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the Calculation**:\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Amount Spent} = 10\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, Edward spent $10."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Information:**\n   - Let \\( D \\) represent the number of marbles Doug has.\n   - Initially, Ed has 19 more marbles than Doug. Therefore, Ed has \\( D + 19 \\) marbles.\n\n2. **After Losing Marbles:**\n   - Ed loses some marbles and now has 8 more marbles than Doug.\n   - Let \\( x \\) represent the number of marbles Ed lost.\n   - After losing marbles, Ed has \\( (D + 19) - x \\) marbles.\n   - According to the problem, after losing marbles, Ed has 8 more marbles than Doug. Therefore, we can write the equation:\n     \\[\n     (D + 19) - x = D + 8\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Simplify the equation:\n     \\[\n     D + 19 - x = D + 8\n     \\]\n   - Subtract \\( D \\) from both sides:\n     \\[\n     19 - x = 8\n     \\]\n   - Subtract 8 from both sides:\n     \\[\n     19 - 8 = x\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the value of \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 11\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Ed lost 11 marbles at the playground.\n\nTherefore, Ed lost 11 marbles."

Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the given information:**\n   - There are 20 houses in a block.\n   - Each house receives 32 pieces of junk mail.\n\n2. **Calculate the total number of pieces of junk mail for the block:**\n   - Multiply the number of houses by the number of pieces of junk mail each house receives.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total pieces of junk mail} = \\text{Number of houses} \\times \\text{Pieces of junk mail per house}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total pieces of junk mail} = 20 \\times 32\n   \\]\n\n3. **Perform the multiplication:**\n\n   \\[\n   20 \\times 32 = 640\n   \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - The mailman should deliver a total of 640 pieces of junk mail to all the houses in the block.\n\nTherefore, the answer is 640 pieces of junk mail."

'To determine how much carpet Jesse needs to cover the floors of all 20 rooms, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the dimensions of one room:**\n   - Each room is 19 feet long and 18 feet wide.\n\n2. **Calculate the area of one room:**\n   - The area of a rectangle is calculated by multiplying its length by its width.\n   - Area of one room = 19 feet * 18 feet = 342 square feet.\n\n3. **Determine the total number of rooms:**\n   - Jesse has 20 rooms in total.\n\n4. **Calculate the total carpet needed for all rooms:**\n   - Multiply the area of one room by the total number of rooms to find the total carpet needed.\n   - Total carpet needed = 342 square feet/room * 20 rooms = 6,840 square feet.\n\nTherefore, Jesse needs 6,840 square feet of carpet to cover the floors of all 20 rooms.'

'To solve the problem, we need to determine how many t-shirts were sold during the Texas Tech game. We can do this by following these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Total t-shirts sold during both games: 242\n   - T-shirts sold during the Arkansas game: 115\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of t-shirts sold during the Texas Tech game.\n   - According to the information, the total number of t-shirts sold during both games is the sum of those sold during the Arkansas game and the Texas Tech game. Therefore, we can write the equation:\n     \\[\n     115 + x = 242\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve for \\( x \\):**\n   - Subtract 115 from both sides of the equation to isolate \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 242 - 115\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the right side:\n     \\[\n     x = 127\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - The Razorback t-shirt shop sold 127 t-shirts during the Texas Tech game.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that 127 t-shirts were sold during the Texas Tech game.'
"To solve the problem, we need to determine how many t-shirts were sold by the Razorback t-shirt shop during the Arkansas and Texas Tech game. We know the following:\n\n1. The shop makes $23 off each t-shirt sold.\n2. They made a total of $230 by selling t-shirts.\n\nLet's solve the problem step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the total revenue and the revenue per t-shirt:**\n   - Total revenue from t-shirt sales = $230\n   - Revenue per t-shirt = $23\n\n2. **Set up the equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of t-shirts sold.\n   - The equation based on the revenue is: \n     \\[\n     23x = 230\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve for \\( x \\):**\n   - Divide both sides of the equation by 23 to find the number of t-shirts sold:\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{230}{23}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the result:**\n   - \\( x = 10 \\)\n\nTherefore, the Razorback t-shirt shop sold 10 t-shirts during the Arkansas and Texas Tech game."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Number of Books:**\n   - Paul initially had 108 books.\n\n2. **Books Given to Friend:**\n   - Paul gave 35 books to his friend.\n\n3. **Books Left After Transactions:**\n   - After selling some books and giving 35 books to his friend, Paul had 62 books left.\n\nNow, let's calculate how many books Paul sold in the garage sale:\n\n- **Step 1:** Calculate the number of books Paul had after giving 35 books to his friend.\n  \\[\n  \\text{Books after giving to friend} = 108 - 35 = 73\n  \\]\n\n- **Step 2:** Calculate the number of books Paul sold in the garage sale.\n  \\[\n  \\text{Books sold} = \\text{Books after giving to friend} - \\text{Books left}\n  \\]\n  \\[\n  \\text{Books sold} = 73 - 62 = 11\n  \\]\n\nTherefore, Paul sold 11 books in the garage sale."

Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the number of large planks:**\n   - John uses 12 large planks of wood.\n\n2. **Identify the number of small planks:**\n   - John uses 17 small planks of wood.\n\n3. **Calculate the total number of planks:**\n   - Total planks = Number of large planks + Number of small planks\n   - Total planks = 12 large planks + 17 small planks\n\n4. **Perform the addition:**\n   - Total planks = 12 + 17 = 29\n\nTherefore, John needs a total of 29 planks for the house wall."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Melissa played 3 games.\n   - She scored a total of 81 points.\n   - She scored the same number of points in each game.\n\n2. **Set Up the Problem:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of points Melissa scored in each game.\n   - Since she scored the same number of points in each game, the total points scored can be expressed as:\n     \\[\n     3x = 81\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve for \\( x \\):**\n   - To find \\( x \\), divide both sides of the equation by 3:\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{81}{3}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the Result:**\n   - Perform the division:\n     \\[\n     x = 27\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Melissa scored 27 points in each game.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Melissa scored 27 points in each game."

'To solve the problem of determining how many seeds Paige and her mom planted in each flowerbed, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Total number of seeds planted: 45\n   - Total number of flowerbeds: 9\n   - Seeds were distributed equally among the flowerbeds.\n\n2. **Set Up the Problem:**\n   - We need to find out how many seeds were planted in each flowerbed. Since the seeds were distributed equally, we can use division to solve this.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Divide the total number of seeds by the total number of flowerbeds to find the number of seeds per flowerbed.\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of seeds per flowerbed} = \\frac{\\text{Total number of seeds}}{\\text{Total number of flowerbeds}} = \\frac{45}{9}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate:**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{45}{9} = 5\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Paige and her mom planted 5 seeds in each flowerbed.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that they planted 5 seeds in each flowerbed.'

'To solve the problem of determining how many cakes the baker made, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - The baker sold 145 cakes.\n   - The baker still has 72 cakes left.\n\n2. **List the Information:**\n   - Cakes sold = 145\n   - Cakes left = 72\n\n3. **Determine the Total Number of Cakes Made:**\n   - To find the total number of cakes the baker made, we need to add the number of cakes sold to the number of cakes left.\n\n4. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total cakes made} = \\text{Cakes sold} + \\text{Cakes left}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total cakes made} = 145 + 72\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total cakes made} = 217\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The baker made a total of 217 cakes.\n\nTherefore, the baker made 217 cakes in total.'
"To find the length of Jesse's room, we can use the formula for the area of a rectangle, which is:\n\n\\[ \\text{Area} = \\text{Width} \\times \\text{Length} \\]\n\nWe are given:\n- The area of the room (carpet needed) is 10 square feet.\n- The width of the room is 2 feet.\n\nWe need to find the length of the room. Let's solve this step by step:\n\n1. **Write down the formula for the area of a rectangle:**\n\n   \\[ \\text{Area} = \\text{Width} \\times \\text{Length} \\]\n\n2. **Substitute the known values into the formula:**\n\n   \\[ 10 = 2 \\times \\text{Length} \\]\n\n3. **Solve for the length:**\n\n   \\[ \\text{Length} = \\frac{10}{2} \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the length:**\n\n   \\[ \\text{Length} = 5 \\]\n\nTherefore, the length of Jesse's room is 5 feet."
"To solve the problem of determining how many bananas are in Philip's collection, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - The bananas are organized into groups.\n   - There are 140 groups.\n   - Each group contains 187 bananas.\n\n2. **List the Information:**\n   - Number of groups = 140\n   - Bananas per group = 187\n\n3. **Calculate the Total Number of Bananas:**\n   - To find the total number of bananas, multiply the number of groups by the number of bananas per group.\n   - Total bananas = Number of groups × Bananas per group\n   - Total bananas = 140 × 187\n\n4. **Perform the Multiplication:**\n   - 140 × 187 = 26,180\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Philip has 26,180 bananas in his collection.\n\nTherefore, the total number of bananas in Philip's collection is 26,180."
"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and question information:\n\n1. **Identify the relevant items**: The problem is focused on the eggs. Rebecca wants to split the eggs into groups of 6. The other items (bananas and marbles) are not relevant to this specific question.\n\n2. **Determine the total number of eggs**: Rebecca has 18 eggs.\n\n3. **Calculate the number of groups**: To find out how many groups of 6 can be created from 18 eggs, we need to divide the total number of eggs by the number of eggs per group.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of groups} = \\frac{\\text{Total number of eggs}}{\\text{Number of eggs per group}} = \\frac{18}{6} = 3\n   \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion**: Rebecca can create 3 groups of 6 eggs each.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Rebecca will create 3 groups."

"To solve the problem, we need to determine the number of visitors to Buckingham Palace over a period of 57 days. We have information about the number of visitors on two specific days, but we need to make some assumptions or gather more data to estimate the total number of visitors over the entire period. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n### Step 1: Understand the Given Information\n- On the day Rachel visited, there were 557 visitors.\n- The previous day had 188 visitors.\n\n### Step 2: List the Known Data\n- Day 1 (Rachel's visit): 557 visitors\n- Day 0 (Previous day): 188 visitors\n\n### Step 3: Assumptions\nSince we only have data for two days, we need to make an assumption about the average number of visitors per day over the 57-day period. One simple assumption is to use the average of the two known days as an estimate for the other days.\n\n### Step 4: Calculate the Average Number of Visitors\n- Average visitors for the two known days = (557 + 188) / 2 = 745 / 2 = 372.5\n\n### Step 5: Estimate Total Visitors Over 57 Days\nAssuming the average number of visitors per day is 372.5, we can estimate the total number of visitors over 57 days:\n\n- Total visitors over 57 days = 372.5 visitors/day * 57 days = 21,232.5\n\nSince the number of visitors must be a whole number, we can round this to the nearest whole number:\n\n- Total estimated visitors = 21,233\n\n### Conclusion\nBased on the assumption that the average number of visitors per day is consistent with the average of the two known days, approximately 21,233 visitors visited Buckingham Palace over the 57-day period."

"To solve the problem, let's break down the information given and follow the steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - The feathers require a total of 288 g of wax.\n   - He currently needs 260 g of wax.\n\n2. **Determine How Much Wax He Already Has:**\n   - If he needs 260 g more to reach the total requirement of 288 g, we can find out how much he already has by subtracting the amount he still needs from the total requirement.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Total wax required = 288 g\n   - Wax needed = 260 g\n   - Wax already have = Total wax required - Wax needed\n   - Wax already have = 288 g - 260 g = 28 g\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - He already has 28 grams of wax.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that he already has 28 grams of wax."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Total number of animals in the cage**: 79\n\n2. **Number of snakes hiding**: 24\n\n3. **Number of alligators hiding**: 51\n\nWe need to find out how many animals were not hiding in the cage.\n\n**Step 1**: Calculate the total number of animals that are hiding.\n\n- Number of snakes hiding: 24\n- Number of alligators hiding: 51\n\nTotal number of animals hiding = Number of snakes hiding + Number of alligators hiding  \nTotal number of animals hiding = 24 + 51 = 75\n\n**Step 2**: Calculate the number of animals that are not hiding.\n\n- Total number of animals in the cage: 79\n- Total number of animals hiding: 75\n\nNumber of animals not hiding = Total number of animals in the cage - Total number of animals hiding  \nNumber of animals not hiding = 79 - 75 = 4\n\nTherefore, the number of animals that were not hiding in the cage is 4."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Book Structure:**\n   - The book has 2 chapters.\n   - Each chapter has 405 pages.\n\n2. **Calculate Total Pages in the Book:**\n   - Total pages = Number of chapters × Pages per chapter\n   - Total pages = 2 chapters × 405 pages/chapter = 810 pages\n\n3. **Determine Reading Duration:**\n   - Frank took 664 days to finish the book.\n\n4. **Calculate Pages Read Per Day:**\n   - Pages per day = Total pages / Total days\n   - Pages per day = 810 pages / 664 days ≈ 1.22 pages/day\n\n5. **Calculate Chapters Read Per Day:**\n   - Since each chapter has 405 pages, we need to find out how many chapters he read per day.\n   - Chapters per day = Pages per day / Pages per chapter\n   - Chapters per day = 1.22 pages/day / 405 pages/chapter ≈ 0.00301 chapters/day\n\nTherefore, Frank read approximately 0.00301 chapters per day."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Number of Roses in the Vase:**\n   - There were initially 2 roses in the vase.\n\n2. **Roses Thrown Away:**\n   - Jessica threw away 4 roses from the vase.\n\n3. **Current Number of Roses in the Vase:**\n   - There are now 23 roses in the vase.\n\n4. **Roses Cut from the Garden:**\n   - We need to find out how many roses Jessica cut from her flower garden to put in the vase.\n\nLet's calculate:\n\n- **Step 1:** Calculate the number of roses in the vase after throwing away 4 roses.\n  - Initial roses = 2\n  - Roses thrown away = 4\n  - Roses left in the vase after throwing away = 2 - 4 = -2\n\n  Since it's not possible to have a negative number of roses, this indicates that the initial information about the number of roses thrown away is incorrect in terms of sequence. Let's adjust our understanding:\n\n- **Step 2:** Consider the logical sequence:\n  - If Jessica threw away 4 roses, she must have added some before or after to reach the current total of 23 roses.\n\n- **Step 3:** Calculate the number of roses Jessica must have added to reach 23 roses:\n  - Current roses in the vase = 23\n  - Initial roses = 2\n  - Roses thrown away = 4\n\n  To find the number of roses she cut and added:\n  - Let \\( x \\) be the number of roses she cut from her garden.\n  - Equation: \\( 2 - 4 + x = 23 \\)\n\n- **Step 4:** Solve the equation:\n  - \\( -2 + x = 23 \\)\n  - \\( x = 23 + 2 \\)\n  - \\( x = 25 \\)\n\nTherefore, Jessica cut 25 roses from her flower garden to put in the vase."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Total**: Bobby ate a total of 43 pieces of candy.\n\n2. **Additional Pieces**: After eating some initially, he ate 25 more pieces.\n\n3. **Core Question**: We need to find out how many pieces of candy Bobby ate initially before eating the additional 25 pieces.\n\nLet's set up an equation to solve this:\n\n- Let \\( x \\) be the number of pieces of candy Bobby ate initially.\n- According to the problem, after eating the initial \\( x \\) pieces, he ate 25 more pieces.\n- The total number of pieces he ate is 43.\n\nSo, we can write the equation as:\n\\[ x + 25 = 43 \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation**:\n   - Subtract 25 from both sides to isolate \\( x \\):\n   \\[ x = 43 - 25 \\]\n   \\[ x = 18 \\]\n\nTherefore, Bobby initially ate 18 pieces of candy before eating the additional 25 pieces."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - They harvest 8 sacks of oranges per day.\n   - The goal is to harvest 24 sacks of oranges.\n\n2. **Determine the Number of Days Needed:**\n   - We need to find out how many days it will take to harvest 24 sacks if 8 sacks are harvested each day.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - To find the number of days required, divide the total number of sacks needed by the number of sacks harvested per day.\n   - Calculation: \\( \\frac{24 \\text{ sacks}}{8 \\text{ sacks/day}} = 3 \\text{ days} \\)\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - It will take 3 days to harvest 24 sacks of oranges if 8 sacks are harvested per day.\n\nTherefore, the answer is 3 days."

"To solve the problem, we need to determine how many trees Haley originally grew in her backyard before the typhoon. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - After the typhoon, 5 trees died.\n   - 12 trees were left after the typhoon.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of trees Haley originally grew.\n   - After the typhoon, 5 trees died, so the number of trees left is \\( x - 5 \\).\n   - We know that 12 trees were left after the typhoon, so we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     x - 5 = 12\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Add 5 to both sides of the equation to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x - 5 + 5 = 12 + 5\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     x = 17\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Haley originally grew 17 trees in her backyard before the typhoon.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Haley originally grew 17 trees."
"To solve the problem, we need to determine how much more a t-shirt costs than a jersey based on the profit made from each item. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Profit from each t-shirt**: $192\n2. **Profit from each jersey**: $34\n\n3. **Core question**: How much more does a t-shirt cost than a jersey?\n\nTo find out how much more a t-shirt costs than a jersey, we subtract the profit from each jersey from the profit from each t-shirt:\n\n\\[ \\text{Difference in cost} = \\text{Profit from each t-shirt} - \\text{Profit from each jersey} \\]\n\n\\[ \\text{Difference in cost} = 192 - 34 \\]\n\n\\[ \\text{Difference in cost} = 158 \\]\n\nTherefore, a t-shirt costs $158 more than a jersey."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Collection:**\n   - Together, Marco and his dad initially collected strawberries weighing 22 pounds.\n\n2. **Marco's Initial Collection:**\n   - Let \\( M \\) be the weight of strawberries Marco initially collected.\n   - Let \\( D \\) be the weight of strawberries Marco's dad initially collected.\n   - We know that \\( M + D = 22 \\).\n\n3. **Marco's Current Collection:**\n   - Marco's strawberries now weigh 36 pounds.\n   - This means Marco found or received additional strawberries, as his initial collection was part of the 22 pounds.\n\n4. **Additional Strawberries Found by Marco's Dad:**\n   - Marco's dad found an additional 30 pounds of strawberries on the way back.\n\n5. **Calculate Marco's Initial Collection:**\n   - Since Marco's strawberries now weigh 36 pounds, and initially, they were part of the 22 pounds, we can deduce that Marco initially had fewer strawberries than he has now.\n   - Let's assume Marco initially had \\( M \\) pounds, and now he has 36 pounds. Therefore, he must have gained \\( 36 - M \\) pounds additionally.\n\n6. **Calculate Marco's Dad's Current Collection:**\n   - Marco's dad initially had \\( D \\) pounds.\n   - He found an additional 30 pounds, so his current collection is \\( D + 30 \\).\n\n7. **Solve for Initial Weights:**\n   - From the equation \\( M + D = 22 \\), we can express \\( D \\) as \\( D = 22 - M \\).\n\n8. **Determine Marco's Initial Collection:**\n   - Since Marco's strawberries now weigh 36 pounds, and he initially had \\( M \\) pounds, we can assume he gained \\( 36 - M \\) pounds additionally.\n   - To find \\( M \\), we need to consider that the total additional strawberries found by both Marco and his dad should equal the difference between their current and initial total weights.\n\n9. **Calculate Marco's Dad's Current Collection:**\n   - Substitute \\( D = 22 - M \\) into the equation for Marco's dad's current collection:\n   \\[\n   D + 30 = (22 - M) + 30 = 52 - M\n   \\]\n\n10. **Determine the Final Weight of Marco's Dad's Strawberries:**\n    - Since Marco's strawberries now weigh 36 pounds, and initially, they were part of the 22 pounds, we can deduce that Marco initially had fewer strawberries than he has now.\n    - Therefore, Marco's dad's strawberries now weigh \\( 52 - M \\).\n\n11. **Conclusion:**\n    - Since Marco's strawberries now weigh 36 pounds, and initially, they were part of the 22 pounds, we can deduce that Marco initially had fewer strawberries than he has now.\n    - Therefore, Marco's dad's strawberries now weigh \\( 52 - 36 = 16 \\) pounds.\n\nThus, Marco's dad's strawberries now weigh 16 pounds."

'To determine how many more push-ups Zachary did than David, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **List the Information:**\n   - Zachary did 51 push-ups.\n   - David did 44 push-ups.\n\n2. **Understand the Question:**\n   - We need to find out how many more push-ups Zachary did compared to David.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Subtract the number of push-ups David did from the number of push-ups Zachary did.\n   - Calculation: \\( 51 - 44 = 7 \\)\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Zachary did 7 more push-ups than David.\n\nTherefore, Zachary did 7 more push-ups than David.'
'To solve the problem of determining how many people each seat on the Ferris wheel can hold, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the given information:**\n   - Total number of people who can ride the Ferris wheel at the same time: 16\n   - Total number of seats on the Ferris wheel: 4\n\n2. **Set up the problem:**\n   - We need to find out how many people can sit in each seat if there are 4 seats and a total of 16 people can ride at the same time.\n\n3. **Perform the calculation:**\n   - To find the number of people each seat can hold, divide the total number of people by the total number of seats.\n   - Calculation: \\( \\frac{16 \\text{ people}}{4 \\text{ seats}} = 4 \\text{ people per seat} \\)\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each seat on the Ferris wheel can hold 4 people.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that each seat can hold 4 people.'

"To determine how much money Lewis earns per week, we need to divide his total earnings by the number of weeks he worked. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Total Earnings**: Lewis earns a total of $460.\n2. **Duration**: The earnings are over a period of 5 weeks.\n3. **Core Question**: We need to find out how much money Lewis earns per week.\n\n**Calculation**:\n\n- To find the weekly earnings, divide the total earnings by the number of weeks:\n  \\[\n  \\text{Weekly Earnings} = \\frac{\\text{Total Earnings}}{\\text{Number of Weeks}} = \\frac{460}{5}\n  \\]\n\n- Perform the division:\n  \\[\n  \\frac{460}{5} = 92\n  \\]\n\nTherefore, Lewis earns $92 per week."

'To solve the problem of how much Edward spent in total on books and pens, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the amounts spent:**\n   - Edward spent $4 on books.\n   - Edward spent $3 on pens.\n\n2. **Calculate the total amount spent:**\n   - Add the amount spent on books to the amount spent on pens:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total spent} = \\text{Amount spent on books} + \\text{Amount spent on pens}\n     \\]\n   - Substitute the known values:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total spent} = 4 + 3\n     \\]\n\n3. **Perform the addition:**\n   - Calculate the sum:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total spent} = 7\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Edward spent a total of $7 on books and pens.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Edward spent $7 in total on books and pens.'
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Edward spent $17.**\n   - This means that before spending, Edward had some amount of money, which we need to find.\n\n2. **Edward received $10 from his friend.**\n   - After spending $17, Edward received an additional $10.\n\n3. **Now Edward has $7.**\n   - This is the amount of money Edward has after spending $17 and receiving $10.\n\nLet's denote the amount of money Edward had initially as \\( x \\).\n\n**Step-by-step calculation:**\n\n- Edward initially had \\( x \\) dollars.\n- He spent $17, so he had \\( x - 17 \\) dollars left.\n- He then received $10 from his friend, so he had \\( x - 17 + 10 \\) dollars.\n- We know that after these transactions, Edward has $7.\n\nSo, we can set up the equation:\n\n\\[ x - 17 + 10 = 7 \\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\n\\[ x - 7 = 7 \\]\n\nAdd 7 to both sides to solve for \\( x \\):\n\n\\[ x = 14 \\]\n\nTherefore, Edward had $14 before he spent his money."

This can be expressed as:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Number of girls} = \\text{Number of boys} + 402\n     \\]\n   - Substitute the number of girls (739) into the equation:\n     \\[\n     739 = B + 402\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the equation for \\( B \\):**\n   - Subtract 402 from both sides of the equation to isolate \\( B \\):\n     \\[\n     739 - 402 = B\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the result:\n     \\[\n     337 = B\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - There are 337 boys in the school.\n\nTherefore, the number of boys in the school is 337."

This means she needs to make 44 necklaces in total.\n\n2. **Necklaces Already Made:** Emily has already made 26 necklaces.\n\n3. **Necklaces Remaining:** To find out how many more necklaces Emily needs to make, subtract the number of necklaces she has already made from the total number of necklaces needed:\n   \\[\n   44 - 26 = 18\n   \\]\n   So, Emily needs to make 18 more necklaces.\n\n4. **Beads per Necklace:** Each necklace requires 2 beads.\n\n5. **Beads Used for Completed Necklaces:** Calculate the number of beads used for the 26 necklaces she has already made:\n   \\[\n   26 \\times 2 = 52\n   \\]\n   Emily has used 52 beads for the necklaces she has already made.\n\n6. **Beads Needed for Remaining Necklaces:** Calculate the number of beads needed for the 18 remaining necklaces:\n   \\[\n   18 \\times 2 = 36\n   \\]\n   Emily needs 36 more beads to complete the remaining necklaces.\n\n7. **Total Beads Initially:** To find out how many beads Emily had initially, add the beads she has already used to the beads she still needs:\n   \\[\n   52 + 36 = 88\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, Emily initially had 88 beads."

Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Total points scored by Melissa: 21 points\n   - Points scored per game: 7 points\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) represent the number of games Melissa played.\n   - Since she scores 7 points per game, the total points scored can be represented by the equation:\n     \\[\n     7 \\times x = 21\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( x \\), divide both sides of the equation by 7:\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{21}{7}\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the division:\n     \\[\n     x = 3\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Melissa played 3 games.\n\nTherefore, Melissa played a total of 3 games."
