'To solve the problem of determining how many bottle caps Danny had initially, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the Information Given:**\n   - Danny found 29 bottle caps at the park.\n   - After finding these bottle caps, Danny has a total of 42 bottle caps in his collection.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of bottle caps Danny had initially.\n   - After finding 29 bottle caps, the total number of bottle caps Danny has is 42.\n\n3. **Formulate the Equation:**\n   \\[\n   x + 29 = 42\n   \\]\n\n4. **Solve for \\( x \\):**\n   - Subtract 29 from both sides of the equation to isolate \\( x \\):\n   \\[\n   x = 42 - 29\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x = 13\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Danny initially had 13 bottle caps in his collection.\n\nTherefore, Danny had 13 bottle caps at first.'
'To solve the problem of determining how many cookies are in each bag, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - You have 4 bags.\n   - The total number of cookies is 36.\n   - Each bag contains an equal number of cookies.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) represent the number of cookies in each bag.\n   - Since there are 4 bags, the total number of cookies can be expressed as \\( 4x \\).\n\n3. **Write the Equation:**\n   - According to the problem, the total number of cookies is 36. Therefore, the equation is:\n     \\[\n     4x = 36\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Divide both sides of the equation by 4 to find \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{36}{4}\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the division:\n     \\[\n     x = 9\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each bag contains 9 cookies.\n\nTherefore, each bag has 9 cookies.'
'To solve the problem of determining how many packages of 13 white t-shirts each mom will have if she buys 39 white t-shirts, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - White t-shirts are sold in packages of 13.\n   - Mom buys a total of 39 white t-shirts.\n   - We need to find out how many packages of 13 t-shirts each she will have.\n\n2. **Set Up the Calculation:**\n   - We need to divide the total number of t-shirts (39) by the number of t-shirts in each package (13).\n\n3. **Perform the Division:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of packages} = \\frac{39}{13}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate:**\n   - Divide 39 by 13:\n     \\[\n     39 \\div 13 = 3\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Mom will have 3 packages of white t-shirts.\n\nTherefore, if mom buys 39 white t-shirts, she will have 3 packages.'
"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and calculate the total number of pupils in the school after the additional girls joined.\n\n1. **Initial number of girls**: 706\n2. **Initial number of boys**: 222\n3. **Additional girls joined**: 418\n\nNow, let's calculate the total number of girls after the additional girls joined:\n\n- Total number of girls = Initial number of girls + Additional girls joined\n- Total number of girls = 706 + 418 = 1,124\n\nNext, calculate the total number of pupils in the school:\n\n- Total number of pupils = Total number of girls + Initial number of boys\n- Total number of pupils = 1,124 + 222 = 1,346\n\nTherefore, there are 1,346 pupils in the school now."
'To determine how many nails John needs to secure the planks for the house wall, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Requirements:**\n   - Each plank requires 2 nails.\n   - John will use 16 planks for the house wall.\n\n2. **Calculate the Total Number of Nails Needed:**\n   - Multiply the number of planks by the number of nails required per plank.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total number of nails} = \\text{Number of planks} \\times \\text{Nails per plank}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total number of nails} = 16 \\times 2\n   \\]\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - \\(16 \\times 2 = 32\\)\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - John needs 32 nails to secure the 16 planks of wood for the house wall.\n\nTherefore, John needs a total of 32 nails.'
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Dave used 8 tickets to buy toys.\n   - Dave used 18 tickets to buy clothes.\n\n2. **Determine the Difference:**\n   - We need to find out how many more tickets Dave used to buy clothes than he did to buy toys.\n\n3. **Calculate the Difference:**\n   - Number of tickets used for clothes: 18\n   - Number of tickets used for toys: 8\n   - Difference in tickets used: \\(18 - 8 = 10\\)\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Dave used 10 more tickets to buy clothes than he did to buy toys.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Dave used 10 more tickets to buy clothes than he did to buy toys."
"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint:\n\n1. **Understand the total weight of strawberries:**\n   - Together, Marco and his dad's strawberries weighed 35 pounds.\n\n2. **Know Marco's strawberry weight:**\n   - Marco's strawberries weighed 13 pounds.\n\n3. **Calculate the weight of Marco's dad's strawberries:**\n   - Since the total weight of the strawberries is 35 pounds and Marco's strawberries weigh 13 pounds, we can find the weight of Marco's dad's strawberries by subtracting Marco's weight from the total weight.\n   - Weight of Marco's dad's strawberries = Total weight - Marco's weight\n   - Weight of Marco's dad's strawberries = 35 pounds - 13 pounds = 22 pounds\n\n4. **Determine how much more Marco's dad's strawberries weigh than Marco's:**\n   - To find out how much more Marco's dad's strawberries weigh than Marco's, subtract Marco's strawberry weight from his dad's strawberry weight.\n   - Difference in weight = Dad's strawberry weight - Marco's strawberry weight\n   - Difference in weight = 22 pounds - 13 pounds = 9 pounds\n\nTherefore, Marco's dad's strawberries weigh 9 pounds more than Marco's strawberries."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the machine's production rate:**\n   - The industrial machine can make 3 shirts per minute.\n\n2. **Calculate the time taken to make shirts yesterday:**\n   - The machine made 4 shirts yesterday.\n   - To find out how many minutes it took, divide the number of shirts by the production rate:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Time for yesterday} = \\frac{4 \\text{ shirts}}{3 \\text{ shirts/minute}} = \\frac{4}{3} \\text{ minutes} \\approx 1.33 \\text{ minutes}\n     \\]\n\n3. **Calculate the time taken to make shirts today:**\n   - The machine made 8 shirts today.\n   - To find out how many minutes it took, divide the number of shirts by the production rate:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Time for today} = \\frac{8 \\text{ shirts}}{3 \\text{ shirts/minute}} = \\frac{8}{3} \\text{ minutes} \\approx 2.67 \\text{ minutes}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the total time worked:**\n   - Add the time taken for yesterday and today:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total time} = \\frac{4}{3} \\text{ minutes} + \\frac{8}{3} \\text{ minutes} = \\frac{12}{3} \\text{ minutes} = 4 \\text{ minutes}\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, the industrial machine worked for a total of 4 minutes to make 4 shirts yesterday and 8 shirts today."
'To solve the problem of finding how many more red peaches there are than yellow peaches in the basket, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the number of each type of peach:**\n   - Number of red peaches: 19\n   - Number of yellow peaches: 11\n\n2. **Understand the core question:**\n   - We need to find out how many more red peaches there are compared to yellow peaches.\n\n3. **Calculate the difference:**\n   - Subtract the number of yellow peaches from the number of red peaches:\n     \\[\n     19 \\, (\\text{red peaches}) - 11 \\, (\\text{yellow peaches}) = 8\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - There are 8 more red peaches than yellow peaches in the basket.\n\nTherefore, the answer is 8.'

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Total Trees Initially**: Haley grew 13 trees in her backyard.\n\n2. **Trees that Died**: After the typhoon, 6 trees died.\n\n3. **Trees that Survived**: To find out how many trees survived, subtract the number of trees that died from the total number of trees:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Trees that survived} = 13 - 6 = 7\n   \\]\n\n4. **Comparison**: Now, we need to determine how many more trees survived than those that died. This involves comparing the number of trees that survived to the number that died:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Difference} = \\text{Trees that survived} - \\text{Trees that died} = 7 - 6 = 1\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, 1 more tree survived the typhoon than those that died."

'To solve the problem of determining how many baseball cards Nell had initially, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Nell gave 301 baseball cards to Jeff.\n   - After giving away the cards, Nell has 154 cards left.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of baseball cards Nell had initially.\n   - After giving away 301 cards, Nell has 154 cards left. This can be expressed as:\n     \\[\n     x - 301 = 154\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( x \\), add 301 to both sides of the equation:\n     \\[\n     x - 301 + 301 = 154 + 301\n     \\]\n   - Simplify the equation:\n     \\[\n     x = 455\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Nell initially had 455 baseball cards.\n\nTherefore, Nell had 455 baseball cards initially.'

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Number of Books:**\n   - Paul initially had 71 books.\n\n2. **Books Bought:**\n   - Paul bought 38 new books.\n\n3. **Final Number of Books:**\n   - Paul has 116 books now.\n\n4. **Books Sold:**\n   - To find out how many books Paul sold, we can use the equation:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Initial Books} - \\text{Books Sold} + \\text{Books Bought} = \\text{Final Books}\n     \\]\n     Plugging in the numbers:\n     \\[\n     71 - \\text{Books Sold} + 38 = 116\n     \\]\n\n5. **Solve for Books Sold:**\n   - Simplify the equation:\n     \\[\n     71 + 38 - \\text{Books Sold} = 116\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     109 - \\text{Books Sold} = 116\n     \\]\n   - Rearrange to find the number of books sold:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Books Sold} = 109 - 116\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     \\text{Books Sold} = -7\n     \\]\n   - Since the number of books sold cannot be negative, let's correct the calculation:\n     \\[\n     71 + 38 = 109\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     109 - \\text{Books Sold} = 116\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     \\text{Books Sold} = 109 - 116\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     \\text{Books Sold} = 7\n     \\]\n\n6. **Books Bought vs. Books Sold:**\n   - Paul bought 38 books and sold 7 books.\n   - The difference between books bought and books sold is:\n     \\[\n     38 - 7 = 31\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, Paul bought 31 more books than he sold."

'To solve the problem of determining how many erasers are in each group when 4950 erasers are organized into 495 groups, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Total number of erasers: 4950\n   - Number of groups: 495\n   - We need to find out how many erasers are in each group.\n\n2. **Set Up the Calculation:**\n   - To find the number of erasers per group, we need to divide the total number of erasers by the number of groups.\n\n3. **Perform the Division:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of erasers per group} = \\frac{\\text{Total number of erasers}}{\\text{Number of groups}} = \\frac{4950}{495}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate:**\n   - Perform the division: \n     \\[\n     4950 \\div 495 = 10\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each group contains 10 erasers.\n\nTherefore, when 4950 erasers are organized into 495 groups, each group contains 10 erasers.'
"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Identify the Variables:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of students who suggested adding bacon.\n\n2. **Understand the Relationships:**\n   - According to the problem, 457 students suggested adding mashed potatoes.\n   - It is also stated that 63 more students suggested adding mashed potatoes than those who suggested bacon.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Since 63 more students suggested mashed potatoes than bacon, we can express this relationship as:\n     \\[\n     x + 63 = 457\n     \\]\n   - Here, \\( x + 63 \\) represents the number of students who suggested mashed potatoes, which is given as 457.\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( x \\), subtract 63 from both sides of the equation:\n     \\[\n     x + 63 = 457\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     x = 457 - 63\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     x = 394\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Therefore, 394 students suggested adding bacon to the menu.\n\nThe answer is that 394 students suggested adding bacon."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided in the hint:\n\n1. **Original Price of Each T-shirt**: $51\n2. **Discount Offered per T-shirt**: $8\n3. **Discounted Price of Each T-shirt**: $51 - $8 = $43\n4. **Number of T-shirts Sold**: 130\n\nNow, we need to calculate the total revenue from selling the t-shirts at the discounted price:\n\n5. **Total Revenue Calculation**:  \n   - Discounted Price per T-shirt = $43\n   - Number of T-shirts Sold = 130\n   - Total Revenue = Discounted Price per T-shirt × Number of T-shirts Sold  \n   - Total Revenue = $43 × 130 = $5,590\n\nTherefore, the Razorback t-shirt shop made $5,590 from selling 130 t-shirts at a discounted price of $43 each during the Arkansas and Texas Tech game."

"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and question information:\n\n1. **Understand the Total Number of Pages:**\n   - The book has a total of 555 pages.\n\n2. **Understand the Number of Chapters:**\n   - The book is divided into 5 chapters.\n\n3. **Pages are Equally Distributed:**\n   - The pages are equally distributed over the 5 chapters.\n\n4. **Calculate the Number of Pages per Chapter:**\n   - Since the pages are equally distributed, we need to divide the total number of pages by the number of chapters to find out how many pages are in each chapter.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Pages per chapter} = \\frac{\\text{Total pages}}{\\text{Number of chapters}} = \\frac{555}{5}\n   \\]\n\n5. **Perform the Division:**\n   - \\(\\frac{555}{5} = 111\\)\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each chapter has 111 pages.\n\nTherefore, each chapter of the book contains 111 pages."

"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and perform the necessary calculations:\n\n1. **Original cost of each pack of DVDs**: $107\n\n2. **Discount on each pack**: $106\n\n3. **Cost of each pack after discount**:  \n   \\[\n   \\text{Cost after discount} = \\text{Original cost} - \\text{Discount} = 107 - 106 = 1 \\text{ dollar}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Total amount available to spend**: $93\n\n5. **Calculate the number of packs you can buy**:  \n   Since each pack costs $1 after the discount, you can buy as many packs as the total amount of money you have, which is $93.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of packs} = \\frac{\\text{Total amount available}}{\\text{Cost per pack after discount}} = \\frac{93}{1} = 93\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, you can buy 93 packs of DVDs with $93."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Melissa scored 12 points in each game.\n   - She scored a total of 36 points.\n\n2. **Define the Problem:**\n   - We need to find out how many games Melissa played.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of games Melissa played.\n   - Since she scored 12 points in each game, the total points scored can be represented as \\( 12 \\times x \\).\n   - We know the total points scored is 36.\n\n4. **Write the Equation:**\n   \\[\n   12 \\times x = 36\n   \\]\n\n5. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( x \\), divide both sides of the equation by 12:\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{36}{12}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x = 3\n   \\]\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - Melissa played 3 games.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Melissa played 3 games."

"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint:\n\n1. **Understand the total number of crackers Matthew had:**\n   - Matthew had a total of 8 crackers.\n\n2. **Understand how many crackers each friend received:**\n   - Each friend received 2 crackers.\n\n3. **Determine how many friends received crackers:**\n   - We need to find out how many friends Matthew gave crackers to, given that each friend received 2 crackers.\n\n4. **Set up the equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of friends Matthew gave crackers to.\n   - Since each friend received 2 crackers, the total number of crackers given out is \\( 2 \\times x \\).\n\n5. **Solve the equation:**\n   - The total number of crackers given out is equal to the total number of crackers Matthew had, which is 8.\n   - Therefore, the equation is: \\( 2 \\times x = 8 \\).\n\n6. **Solve for \\( x \\):**\n   \\[\n   2x = 8\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{8}{2}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x = 4\n   \\]\n\n7. **Conclusion:**\n   - Matthew gave crackers to 4 friends.\n\nTherefore, Matthew gave crackers to 4 friends."
"To solve the problem, we need to determine the total number of unique campers who participated in either rowing or hiking throughout the day. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Morning Activities:**\n   - 41 campers went rowing.\n   - 4 campers went hiking.\n\n2. **Afternoon Activities:**\n   - 26 campers went rowing.\n\n3. **Objective:**\n   - Find the total number of unique campers who participated in either rowing or hiking throughout the day.\n\n### Step-by-Step Solution:\n\n1. **Identify Total Rowing Participants:**\n   - In the morning, 41 campers went rowing.\n   - In the afternoon, 26 campers went rowing.\n   - Some campers might have rowed both in the morning and afternoon, so we need to consider the possibility of overlap.\n\n2. **Identify Total Hiking Participants:**\n   - 4 campers went hiking in the morning.\n   - There is no mention of hiking in the afternoon, so we assume no additional hikers.\n\n3. **Determine Unique Participants:**\n   - Since we don't have information about any overlap between morning and afternoon rowing, we assume the worst-case scenario where all afternoon rowers are different from morning rowers.\n   - Therefore, the maximum number of unique rowers is the sum of morning and afternoon rowers: \\(41 + 26 = 67\\).\n\n4. **Combine Rowing and Hiking Participants:**\n   - We need to combine the unique rowers with the hikers.\n   - Since the problem does not specify any overlap between rowers and hikers, we assume they are separate groups.\n   - Therefore, the total number of unique campers is the sum of unique rowers and hikers: \\(67 + 4 = 71\\).\n\n### Conclusion:\n\nThe total number of unique campers who participated in either rowing or hiking throughout the day is 71."

"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Situation:**\n   - There were initially 15 roses in the vase.\n\n2. **Roses Thrown Away:**\n   - Jessica threw away 33 roses from the vase.\n\n3. **Final Situation:**\n   - There are now 17 roses in the vase.\n\n4. **Roses Cut from the Garden:**\n   - We need to determine how many roses Jessica cut from her flower garden to reach the final count of 17 roses in the vase.\n\nLet's calculate the number of roses Jessica cut from her garden:\n\n- **Step 1:** Calculate the number of roses left after throwing away 33 roses.\n  \\[\n  \\text{Roses left after throwing away} = 15 - 33 = -18\n  \\]\n  Since it's not possible to have a negative number of roses in the vase, this indicates that Jessica must have added roses from her garden to reach the final count.\n\n- **Step 2:** Calculate the number of roses needed to reach 17 roses in the vase.\n  \\[\n  \\text{Roses needed to reach 17} = 17 - (-18) = 17 + 18 = 35\n  \\]\n  Therefore, Jessica must have cut 35 roses from her garden.\n\n- **Step 3:** Determine how many more roses Jessica cut than those she threw away.\n  \\[\n  \\text{Roses cut more than thrown away} = 35 - 33 = 2\n  \\]\n\nThus, Jessica cut 2 more roses from her flower garden than the 33 roses she threw away."

To do this, we can use the following steps:\n\n- **Step 1**: Identify the total number of campers who went rowing during the entire day. This is given as 46.\n\n- **Step 2**: Identify the number of campers who went rowing in the morning. This is given as 43.\n\n- **Step 3**: To find the number of campers who went rowing in the afternoon, subtract the number of campers who went in the morning from the total number of campers who went rowing during the day.\n\n  \\[\n  \\text{Number of campers in the afternoon} = \\text{Total campers} - \\text{Campers in the morning}\n  \\]\n\n  \\[\n  \\text{Number of campers in the afternoon} = 46 - 43\n  \\]\n\n- **Step 4**: Perform the subtraction.\n\n  \\[\n  \\text{Number of campers in the afternoon} = 3\n  \\]\n\nTherefore, 3 campers went rowing in the afternoon."

"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Situation:**\n   - Let \\( D \\) be the initial number of marbles Doug had.\n   - Ed had 2 more marbles than Doug, so Ed had \\( D + 2 \\) marbles.\n\n2. **After Doug Lost Some Marbles:**\n   - Doug lost some marbles, let's say he lost \\( x \\) marbles.\n   - Now, Doug has \\( D - x \\) marbles.\n\n3. **Current Situation:**\n   - Ed now has 19 more marbles than Doug.\n   - Therefore, \\( D + 2 = (D - x) + 19 \\).\n\n4. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   \\[\n   D + 2 = D - x + 19\n   \\]\n\n5. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Subtract \\( D \\) from both sides:\n     \\[\n     2 = -x + 19\n     \\]\n   - Subtract 19 from both sides:\n     \\[\n     2 - 19 = -x\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     -17 = -x\n     \\]\n   - Multiply both sides by -1 to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 17\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, Doug lost 17 marbles."
'To solve the problem of determining how many skittles are in each group when 896 skittles are organized into 8 groups, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the Total Number of Skittles:**\n   - Total skittles = 896\n\n2. **Identify the Number of Groups:**\n   - Number of groups = 8\n\n3. **Calculate the Number of Skittles per Group:**\n   - To find out how many skittles are in each group, divide the total number of skittles by the number of groups.\n   - Calculation: \\( \\frac{896}{8} \\)\n\n4. **Perform the Division:**\n   - \\( 896 \\div 8 = 112 \\)\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each group contains 112 skittles.\n\nTherefore, when 896 skittles are organized into 8 groups, each group will have 112 skittles.'

'To solve the problem of how many pages Frank read per day, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the given information:**\n   - The book has a total of 612 pages.\n   - Frank took 6 days to finish the book.\n\n2. **Determine the number of pages read per day:**\n   - To find out how many pages Frank read each day, we need to divide the total number of pages by the number of days it took him to finish the book.\n\n3. **Perform the calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Pages per day} = \\frac{\\text{Total pages}}{\\text{Number of days}} = \\frac{612}{6}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the result:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Pages per day} = 102\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, Frank read 102 pages per day.'

'To determine how many weeks the harvest lasted, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Lewis earns $2 every week during the harvest.\n   - His total earnings are $178.\n   - We need to find out how many weeks he worked to earn this amount.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( w \\) represent the number of weeks the harvest lasted.\n   - Since Lewis earns $2 per week, his total earnings can be expressed as \\( 2w \\).\n   - We know his total earnings are $178, so we can set up the equation: \n     \\[\n     2w = 178\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( w \\), divide both sides of the equation by 2:\n     \\[\n     w = \\frac{178}{2}\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the division:\n     \\[\n     w = 89\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - The harvest lasted for 89 weeks.\n\nTherefore, Lewis worked for 89 weeks during the harvest.'

Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the daily harvest of unripe oranges:**\n   - They harvest 24 sacks of unripe oranges per day.\n\n2. **Determine the duration of the harvest:**\n   - The harvest lasts for 45 days.\n\n3. **Calculate the total number of sacks of unripe oranges:**\n   - Multiply the number of sacks harvested per day by the number of days.\n   - Total sacks of unripe oranges = 24 sacks/day × 45 days\n\n4. **Perform the calculation:**\n   - Total sacks of unripe oranges = 24 × 45 = 1080\n\nTherefore, after 45 days of harvest, they will have 1,080 sacks of unripe oranges."

Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the revenue per jersey:**\n   - The Razorback shop makes $165 off each jersey.\n\n2. **Identify the number of jerseys sold:**\n   - They sold 156 jerseys during the Arkansas and Texas Tech game.\n\n3. **Calculate the total revenue from jerseys:**\n   - Multiply the number of jerseys sold by the revenue per jersey:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total revenue from jerseys} = \\text{Number of jerseys sold} \\times \\text{Revenue per jersey}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total revenue from jerseys} = 156 \\times 165\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the multiplication:**\n   \\[\n   156 \\times 165 = 25,740\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the Razorback shop made $25,740 from selling the jerseys during the Arkansas and Texas Tech game."

Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the given information:**\n   - Total number of pots: 466\n   - Number of flowers per pot: 53\n   - Number of sticks per pot: 181\n\n2. **Calculate the total number of flowers:**\n   - Multiply the number of flowers per pot by the total number of pots:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total flowers} = 53 \\times 466\n     \\]\n\n3. **Calculate the total number of sticks:**\n   - Multiply the number of sticks per pot by the total number of pots:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total sticks} = 181 \\times 466\n     \\]\n\n4. **Perform the calculations:**\n\n   - For the total number of flowers:\n     \\[\n     53 \\times 466 = 24,698\n     \\]\n\n   - For the total number of sticks:\n     \\[\n     181 \\times 466 = 84,346\n     \\]\n\n5. **Summarize the results:**\n   - Total number of flowers: 24,698\n   - Total number of sticks: 84,346\n\nTherefore, there are 24,698 flowers and 84,346 sticks in total across all 466 pots."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Capacity of the Ferris Wheel:**\n   - The Ferris wheel has 6 seats.\n   - Each seat can hold 14 people.\n\n2. **Calculate the Total Capacity:**\n   - Total capacity = Number of seats × Capacity per seat\n   - Total capacity = 6 seats × 14 people/seat = 84 people\n\n3. **Determine the Current Occupancy:**\n   - There are currently 16 people on the wheel.\n\n4. **Calculate How Many More People Can Join:**\n   - Available capacity = Total capacity - Current occupancy\n   - Available capacity = 84 people - 16 people = 68 people\n\nTherefore, 68 more people can join the Ferris wheel."

Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Total number of water bottles:** 153\n2. **Number of days the bottles lasted:** 17\n3. **Number of bottles consumed each day:** This is what we need to find.\n\nTo find the number of bottles Debby drank each day, we use the formula:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Number of bottles per day} = \\frac{\\text{Total number of bottles}}{\\text{Number of days}}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the given values into the formula:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Number of bottles per day} = \\frac{153}{17}\n\\]\n\nNow, perform the division:\n\n\\[\n153 \\div 17 = 9\n\\]\n\nTherefore, Debby drank 9 water bottles each day."

"To solve this problem, we need to calculate Lewis's total earnings over the 1181-week harvest season and then subtract his total rent payments over the same period. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Calculate Total Earnings:**\n   - Lewis earns $491 every week.\n   - The harvest season lasts for 1181 weeks.\n   - Total earnings = Weekly earnings × Number of weeks\n   - Total earnings = $491 × 1181\n\n2. **Calculate Total Rent Payments:**\n   - Lewis pays $216 in rent every week.\n   - Total rent payments = Weekly rent × Number of weeks\n   - Total rent payments = $216 × 1181\n\n3. **Calculate Remaining Money:**\n   - Remaining money = Total earnings - Total rent payments\n\nNow, let's do the calculations:\n\n1. **Total Earnings:**\n   \\[\n   491 \\times 1181 = 579,871\n   \\]\n\n2. **Total Rent Payments:**\n   \\[\n   216 \\times 1181 = 255,096\n   \\]\n\n3. **Remaining Money:**\n   \\[\n   579,871 - 255,096 = 324,775\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, Lewis will have $324,775 at the end of the 1181-week harvest season after paying $216 in rent each week."

'To solve the problem of how many pens Paul sold in the garage sale, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the initial number of pens:**\n   - Paul initially had 42 pens.\n\n2. **Identify the number of pens left after the garage sale:**\n   - After the garage sale, Paul had 19 pens left.\n\n3. **Calculate the number of pens sold:**\n   - Subtract the number of pens left from the initial number of pens to find out how many pens were sold.\n   \\[\n   \\text{Pens sold} = \\text{Initial pens} - \\text{Pens left}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Pens sold} = 42 - 19\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Pens sold} = 23\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, Paul sold 23 pens in the garage sale.'

"Let's solve the problem step by step:\n\n1. **Initial Amount of Money:**\n   - Dan initially has $4.\n\n2. **Cost of Each Candy Bar:**\n   - Each candy bar costs $3.\n\n3. **Number of Candy Bars Bought:**\n   - Dan bought 99 candy bars.\n\n4. **Total Cost of Candy Bars:**\n   - To find the total cost of the candy bars, multiply the number of candy bars by the cost of each candy bar:\n     \\[\n     99 \\text{ candy bars} \\times \\$3 \\text{ per candy bar} = \\$297\n     \\]\n\n5. **Amount of Money Left:**\n   - Dan initially had $4, and he spent $297 on candy bars. To find out how much money he has left, subtract the total cost of the candy bars from the initial amount of money:\n     \\[\n     \\$4 - \\$297 = -\\$293\n     \\]\n\nDan does not have enough money to buy 99 candy bars, as he would need $297, but he only has $4. Therefore, he would be short by $293."
"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Number of Children on the Bus:**\n   - Initially, there were 5 children on the bus.\n\n2. **Children Getting Off the Bus:**\n   - 63 children got off the bus.\n\n3. **Children Getting On the Bus:**\n   - After some children got on the bus, there were 14 children altogether on the bus.\n\nNow, let's calculate the number of children who got on the bus:\n\n- **Calculate the Number of Children Remaining After Some Got Off:**\n  - Initially, there were 5 children on the bus.\n  - 63 children got off the bus.\n  - Since 63 children cannot get off if there were only 5 initially, it implies that more children must have been on the bus before they got off. This suggests that the problem might have a logical inconsistency, but let's proceed with the given numbers.\n\n- **Calculate the Number of Children Who Got On:**\n  - After 63 children got off, the number of children on the bus would be \\(5 - 63 = -58\\). This negative number indicates that the initial number of children on the bus was not sufficient to allow 63 to get off, which is a logical inconsistency.\n  - However, we know that after some children got on, there were 14 children on the bus.\n\n- **Determine the Number of Children Who Got On:**\n  - Let \\(x\\) be the number of children who got on the bus.\n  - The equation becomes: \\(-58 + x = 14\\).\n  - Solving for \\(x\\), we get: \\(x = 14 + 58 = 72\\).\n\n4. **Calculate How Many More Children Got On Than Got Off:**\n   - 72 children got on the bus.\n   - 63 children got off the bus.\n   - The difference is \\(72 - 63 = 9\\).\n\nTherefore, 9 more children got on the bus than those that got off."
'To determine how many days the 180 water bottles would last if Debby drinks 15 water bottles per day, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the total number of water bottles:**\n   - Debby bought 180 water bottles.\n\n2. **Determine the daily consumption of water bottles:**\n   - Debby drinks 15 water bottles per day.\n\n3. **Calculate the number of days the water bottles will last:**\n   - To find out how many days the water bottles will last, divide the total number of water bottles by the number of water bottles consumed per day.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of days} = \\frac{\\text{Total water bottles}}{\\text{Water bottles consumed per day}} = \\frac{180}{15}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the division:**\n   - \\(\\frac{180}{15} = 12\\)\n\nTherefore, the 180 water bottles would last for 12 days if Debby drinks 15 water bottles per day.'
"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Recipe Requirements:**\n   - The recipe calls for 3 cups of sugar.\n   - The recipe calls for 10 cups of flour.\n\n2. **Understand the Current Situation:**\n   - Mary still needs 5 more cups of flour than sugar.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of cups of flour Mary has already put in.\n   - The total amount of flour needed is 10 cups.\n   - Therefore, the amount of flour still needed is \\( 10 - x \\).\n\n4. **Relate Flour and Sugar Needs:**\n   - Mary still needs 5 more cups of flour than sugar.\n   - Since the recipe calls for 3 cups of sugar, she still needs 3 cups of sugar.\n   - Therefore, the amount of flour she still needs is \\( 3 + 5 = 8 \\) cups.\n\n5. **Set Up the Equation Based on the Above Information:**\n   - The amount of flour still needed is \\( 10 - x \\).\n   - We know from the problem that this amount is 8 cups.\n   - Therefore, we can set up the equation: \n     \\[\n     10 - x = 8\n     \\]\n\n6. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Subtract 8 from both sides:\n     \\[\n     10 - x = 8 \\implies x = 10 - 8\n     \\]\n   - Simplify:\n     \\[\n     x = 2\n     \\]\n\n7. **Conclusion:**\n   - Mary has already put in 2 cups of flour.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Mary has already put in 2 cups of flour."
"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and perform the necessary calculations:\n\n1. **Determine the total number of pencils:**\n   - Faye has 35 packs of pencils.\n   - Each pack contains 4 pencils.\n   - Total number of pencils = 35 packs × 4 pencils per pack = 140 pencils.\n\n2. **Determine how many rows Faye can make:**\n   - Faye is placing pencils into rows with 2 pencils in each row.\n   - To find out how many rows she can make, divide the total number of pencils by the number of pencils per row.\n   - Number of rows = Total number of pencils ÷ Number of pencils per row = 140 pencils ÷ 2 pencils per row = 70 rows.\n\nTherefore, Faye can make 70 rows of 2 pencils each with a total of 140 pencils."

Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Determine the number of seats per Ferris wheel:**\n   - Each Ferris wheel has 19 seats.\n\n2. **Determine the number of people each seat can hold:**\n   - Each seat can hold 15 people.\n\n3. **Calculate the total number of people one Ferris wheel can hold:**\n   - Multiply the number of seats by the number of people each seat can hold:\n     \\[\n     19 \\text{ seats} \\times 15 \\text{ people per seat} = 285 \\text{ people per Ferris wheel}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the total number of people 20 Ferris wheels can hold:**\n   - Multiply the number of people one Ferris wheel can hold by the number of Ferris wheels:\n     \\[\n     285 \\text{ people per Ferris wheel} \\times 20 \\text{ Ferris wheels} = 5700 \\text{ people}\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, 20 Ferris wheels can hold a total of 5700 people at the same time."

"To solve the problem, we need to determine how many more visitors visited Buckingham Palace on the day with 705 visitors compared to the total number of visitors over the previous 245 days. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the number of visitors on the day in question:**\n   - On the day in question, there were 705 visitors.\n\n2. **Calculate the total number of visitors over the previous 245 days:**\n   - We know the number of visitors for the two days immediately preceding the day in question:\n     - The previous day had 191 visitors.\n     - The day before that had 457 visitors.\n   - Therefore, the number of visitors for the remaining 243 days (245 - 2) is unknown and not provided in the problem. We will assume that the number of visitors for these 243 days is zero for the purpose of this calculation, as no other information is given.\n\n3. **Calculate the total number of visitors over the previous 245 days:**\n   - Total visitors for the previous 245 days = 191 (previous day) + 457 (day before previous) + 0 (remaining 243 days) = 648 visitors.\n\n4. **Calculate the difference in the number of visitors:**\n   - Difference = Number of visitors on the day in question - Total visitors over the previous 245 days\n   - Difference = 705 - 648 = 57\n\nTherefore, there were 57 more visitors on the day with 705 visitors than on the previous 245 days combined."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Information Given:**\n   - Marco's dad's strawberries weighed 11 pounds.\n   - Together, Marco and his dad's strawberries weighed 30 pounds.\n\n2. **Objective:**\n   - Find out how much Marco's strawberries weighed.\n\n3. **Steps to Solve:**\n   - We know the total weight of the strawberries picked by both Marco and his dad is 30 pounds.\n   - We also know that Marco's dad's strawberries weighed 11 pounds.\n   - To find the weight of Marco's strawberries, we need to subtract the weight of his dad's strawberries from the total weight.\n\n4. **Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Weight of Marco's strawberries} = \\text{Total weight} - \\text{Weight of Dad's strawberries}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Weight of Marco's strawberries} = 30 \\text{ pounds} - 11 \\text{ pounds} = 19 \\text{ pounds}\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Marco's strawberries weighed 19 pounds.\n\nTherefore, Marco's strawberries weighed 19 pounds."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Information Given:**\n   - Marco's strawberries weighed 15 pounds.\n   - Together, Marco and his dad's strawberries weighed 37 pounds.\n\n2. **Objective:**\n   - Find out how much Marco's dad's strawberries weighed.\n\n3. **Approach:**\n   - We can use a simple subtraction to find the weight of Marco's dad's strawberries.\n\n4. **Calculation:**\n   - Total weight of strawberries (Marco + Dad) = 37 pounds\n   - Weight of Marco's strawberries = 15 pounds\n   - Weight of Dad's strawberries = Total weight - Marco's weight\n\n5. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Weight of Dad's strawberries} = 37 \\text{ pounds} - 15 \\text{ pounds} = 22 \\text{ pounds}\n   \\]\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - Marco's dad's strawberries weighed 22 pounds.\n\nTherefore, Marco's dad's strawberries weighed 22 pounds."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Shirley sold 10 boxes of trefoils.\n   - She needs to deliver 5 cases of boxes.\n\n2. **Determine the Number of Boxes per Case:**\n   - We need to find out how many boxes are in each case.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - If Shirley sold 10 boxes and these 10 boxes are equivalent to 5 cases, we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total boxes} = \\text{Number of cases} \\times \\text{Boxes per case}\n     \\]\n   - Here, the total number of boxes is 10, and the number of cases is 5.\n\n4. **Solve for Boxes per Case:**\n   - Plug the known values into the equation:\n     \\[\n     10 = 5 \\times \\text{Boxes per case}\n     \\]\n   - To find the number of boxes per case, divide both sides by 5:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Boxes per case} = \\frac{10}{5} = 2\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - There are 2 boxes in each case.\n\nTherefore, Shirley needs to deliver 5 cases, and each case contains 2 boxes."

"To solve the problem, let's break down the information given and follow the steps:\n\n1. **Initial Information:**\n   - Danny found 10 bottle caps at the park.\n   - Danny found 62 wrappers at the park.\n\n2. **Current Collection:**\n   - Danny now has 27 bottle caps in his collection.\n   - Danny now has 43 wrappers in his collection.\n\n3. **Calculate the Difference:**\n   - We need to find out how many more wrappers than bottle caps Danny has in his collection now.\n\n4. **Steps to Solve:**\n   - Determine the number of wrappers Danny has: 43 wrappers.\n   - Determine the number of bottle caps Danny has: 27 bottle caps.\n   - Calculate the difference between the number of wrappers and bottle caps:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Difference} = \\text{Number of Wrappers} - \\text{Number of Bottle Caps} = 43 - 27\n     \\]\n\n5. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   43 - 27 = 16\n   \\]\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - Danny has 16 more wrappers than bottle caps in his collection now.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Danny has 16 more wrappers than bottle caps."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided in the hints:\n\n1. **Initial Count of Birds:**\n   - There are initially 4 birds sitting on the fence.\n\n2. **Initial Count of Storks:**\n   - There are initially 3 storks sitting on the fence.\n\n3. **Additional Storks Joining:**\n   - 6 more storks come to join the storks already on the fence.\n\nNow, let's calculate the total number of storks and birds on the fence:\n\n- **Total Number of Birds:**\n  - Since no additional birds are mentioned, the total number of birds remains 4.\n\n- **Total Number of Storks:**\n  - Initially, there are 3 storks.\n  - 6 more storks join them.\n  - Total number of storks = 3 (initial) + 6 (additional) = 9 storks.\n\nFinally, we need to find out how many more storks than birds are sitting on the fence:\n\n- **Difference in Number:**\n  - Total storks = 9\n  - Total birds = 4\n  - Difference = 9 (storks) - 4 (birds) = 5\n\nTherefore, there are 5 more storks than birds sitting on the fence."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Weight:**\n   - Jessie's initial weight was 114 kilograms.\n\n2. **Weight Loss in the First Week:**\n   - Jessie lost 50 kilograms in the first week.\n\n3. **Weight Loss in the Second Week:**\n   - Jessie lost 60 kilograms in the second week.\n\nNow, let's calculate Jessie's weight after these losses:\n\n- **After the First Week:**\n  - Initial weight: 114 kg\n  - Weight loss in the first week: 50 kg\n  - Weight after the first week = 114 kg - 50 kg = 64 kg\n\n- **After the Second Week:**\n  - Weight after the first week: 64 kg\n  - Weight loss in the second week: 60 kg\n  - Weight after the second week = 64 kg - 60 kg = 4 kg\n\nTherefore, after losing 50 kilograms in the first week and 60 kilograms in the second week, Jessie's weight is now 4 kilograms. 'To find out how much each pack of DVDs costs, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the given information:**\n   - Total cost for 6 packs of DVDs is $120.\n   - Number of packs is 6.\n\n2. **Set up the problem:**\n   - We need to find the cost of one pack of DVDs.\n\n3. **Use the formula for unit cost:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Cost per pack} = \\frac{\\text{Total cost}}{\\text{Number of packs}}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Substitute the given values into the formula:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Cost per pack} = \\frac{120}{6}\n   \\]\n\n5. **Perform the division:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Cost per pack} = 20\n   \\]\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each pack of DVDs costs $20.\n\nTherefore, the cost of each pack of DVDs is $20.'

"To find the total number of people present in the program, we need to add the number of parents, pupils, and teachers together. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Number of parents:** 73\n2. **Number of pupils:** 724\n3. **Number of teachers:** 744\n\nNow, we add these numbers together:\n\n- First, add the number of parents and pupils:\n  \\[\n  73 + 724 = 797\n  \\]\n\n- Next, add the result to the number of teachers:\n  \\[\n  797 + 744 = 1541\n  \\]\n\nTherefore, the total number of people present in the program is 1,541."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Initial Number of People on the Train:**\n   - Initially, there were 11 people on the train.\n\n2. **Number of People Getting On:**\n   - At the stop, 8 more people got on the train.\n\n3. **Calculate the Total Number of People:**\n   - To find the total number of people on the train now, add the initial number of people to the number of people who got on.\n   - Calculation: \\( 11 + 8 = 19 \\)\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - There are now 19 people on the train.\n\nTherefore, the answer is 19 people."
"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and perform the necessary calculations:\n\n1. **Initial Number of Candies:**\n   - Frank initially had 33 pieces of candy.\n\n2. **Candies Lost:**\n   - Frank lost 24 pieces of candy.\n\n3. **Calculate Remaining Candies:**\n   - Subtract the lost candies from the initial number of candies:\n     \\[\n     33 - 24 = 9\n     \\]\n   - Frank has 9 pieces of candy remaining.\n\n4. **Put Remaining Candies into Bags:**\n   - Frank puts the remaining candies into bags with 9 pieces in each bag.\n\n5. **Calculate Number of Bags:**\n   - Since Frank has 9 pieces of candy and each bag holds 9 pieces, he can make:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{9}{9} = 1\n     \\]\n   - Frank can make 1 bag.\n\nTherefore, Frank can make 1 bag with the remaining pieces of candy."
'To solve the problem of determining how many books are in each bookshelf when Bryan has 34 books distributed equally across 2 bookshelves, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the total number of books**:  \n   - Bryan has a total of 34 books.\n\n2. **Identify the number of bookshelves**:  \n   - There are 2 bookshelves.\n\n3. **Understand the distribution**:  \n   - The books are distributed equally across the bookshelves.\n\n4. **Calculate the number of books per bookshelf**:  \n   - To find out how many books are on each bookshelf, divide the total number of books by the number of bookshelves:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of books per bookshelf} = \\frac{\\text{Total number of books}}{\\text{Number of bookshelves}} = \\frac{34}{2} = 17\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion**:  \n   - There are 17 books on each bookshelf.\n\nTherefore, each bookshelf contains 17 books.'
'To solve the problem of determining how many new customers arrived, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the initial number of customers:**\n   - The waiter initially had 3 customers.\n\n2. **Identify the total number of customers after more arrived:**\n   - After some more customers arrived, the waiter had a total of 8 customers.\n\n3. **Calculate the number of new customers:**\n   - To find the number of new customers, subtract the initial number of customers from the total number of customers.\n   - Calculation: \\( 8 \\text{ (total customers)} - 3 \\text{ (initial customers)} = 5 \\text{ (new customers)} \\).\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - The number of new customers that arrived is 5.\n\nTherefore, 5 new customers arrived.'
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Brenda's mother made a total of 38 cookies.\n   - Each guest received 19 cookies.\n\n2. **Determine the Number of Guests:**\n   - We need to find out how many guests received cookies if each guest received 19 cookies.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of guests.\n   - Since each guest received 19 cookies, the total number of cookies distributed to the guests is \\( 19 \\times x \\).\n\n4. **Use the Total Number of Cookies:**\n   - We know the total number of cookies is 38.\n   - Therefore, the equation is: \n     \\[\n     19 \\times x = 38\n     \\]\n\n5. **Solve for \\( x \\):**\n   - Divide both sides of the equation by 19 to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{38}{19}\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the division:\n     \\[\n     x = 2\n     \\]\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - Brenda's mother prepared cookies for 2 guests.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Brenda's mother prepared cookies for 2 guests."

"To solve the problem, we need to determine how many rounds Luke played in the trivia game. We know that he scored a total of 154 points and gained 11 points in each round. Let's break down the problem step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Total points scored by Luke: 154 points\n   - Points gained per round: 11 points\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of rounds Luke played.\n   - Since he gains 11 points per round, the total points can be expressed as:\n     \\[\n     11x = 154\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve for \\( x \\):**\n   - To find the number of rounds, divide the total points by the points per round:\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{154}{11}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Perform the Division:**\n   - Calculate \\( \\frac{154}{11} \\):\n     \\[\n     154 \\div 11 = 14\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Luke played 14 rounds.\n\nTherefore, Luke played a total of 14 rounds to score 154 points, gaining 11 points in each round."
"To solve the problem, let's break down the information given and follow the steps:\n\n1. **List the information:**\n   - Jack received 3 emails in the afternoon.\n   - Jack received 6 emails in the morning.\n   - Jack received a total of 10 emails in the day.\n\n2. **Set up the equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of emails Jack received in the evening.\n   - According to the information, the total number of emails received in the day is the sum of emails received in the morning, afternoon, and evening.\n   - Therefore, the equation is: \n     \\[\n     6 \\, (\\text{morning}) + 3 \\, (\\text{afternoon}) + x \\, (\\text{evening}) = 10 \\, (\\text{total})\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve the equation:**\n   - Combine the known numbers:\n     \\[\n     6 + 3 + x = 10\n     \\]\n   - Simplify the left side:\n     \\[\n     9 + x = 10\n     \\]\n   - Subtract 9 from both sides to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 10 - 9\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     x = 1\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Jack received 1 email in the evening.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Jack received **1 email** in the evening."

"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined below:\n\n1. **Determine the total area of the room:**\n   - The room is 11 feet long and 15 feet wide.\n   - To find the area, multiply the length by the width:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Area of the room} = 11 \\, \\text{feet} \\times 15 \\, \\text{feet} = 165 \\, \\text{square feet}\n     \\]\n\n2. **Identify the amount of carpet Jesse already has:**\n   - Jesse already has 16 square feet of carpet.\n\n3. **Calculate the additional carpet needed:**\n   - Subtract the carpet Jesse already has from the total area of the room to find out how much more carpet is needed:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Additional carpet needed} = 165 \\, \\text{square feet} - 16 \\, \\text{square feet} = 149 \\, \\text{square feet}\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, Jesse needs an additional 149 square feet of carpet to cover the entire floor of her room."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Information:**\n   - Danny threw away 60 old bottle caps.\n   - Danny found 58 new bottle caps.\n   - Danny now has 67 bottle caps in his collection.\n\n2. **Objective:**\n   - Determine how many bottle caps Danny had initially before he threw away 60 and found 58 new ones.\n\n3. **Step-by-Step Calculation:**\n\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of bottle caps Danny had initially.\n   - After throwing away 60 old bottle caps, he would have \\( x - 60 \\) bottle caps.\n   - He then found 58 new bottle caps, so he added these to his collection: \\( (x - 60) + 58 \\).\n   - According to the problem, he now has 67 bottle caps. Therefore, we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     (x - 60) + 58 = 67\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n\n   - Simplify the equation:\n     \\[\n     x - 60 + 58 = 67\n     \\]\n   - Combine like terms:\n     \\[\n     x - 2 = 67\n     \\]\n   - Add 2 to both sides to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 67 + 2\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     x = 69\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Danny initially had 69 bottle caps in his collection.\n\nTherefore, Danny had 69 bottle caps at first."

'To solve the problem of determining how many marbles Josh originally had in his collection, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Josh lost 21 marbles.\n   - Josh currently has 12 marbles.\n\n2. **Determine the Original Number of Marbles:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) represent the original number of marbles Josh had.\n   - According to the problem, after losing 21 marbles, Josh has 12 marbles left.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - The equation based on the information is:\n     \\[\n     x - 21 = 12\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( x \\), add 21 to both sides of the equation:\n     \\[\n     x - 21 + 21 = 12 + 21\n     \\]\n   - Simplifying the equation gives:\n     \\[\n     x = 33\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Josh originally had 33 marbles in his collection.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Josh originally had 33 marbles.'
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the number of aquariums for each type of animal:**\n   - Saltwater aquariums: 15\n   - Freshwater aquariums: 62\n\n2. **Determine the number of animals in each aquarium:**\n   - Each aquarium contains 19 animals.\n\n3. **Calculate the total number of animals in the saltwater aquariums:**\n   - Number of saltwater aquariums × Number of animals per aquarium = Total saltwater animals\n   - \\(15 \\times 19 = 285\\)\n\n4. **Calculate the total number of animals in the freshwater aquariums:**\n   - Number of freshwater aquariums × Number of animals per aquarium = Total freshwater animals\n   - \\(62 \\times 19 = 1,178\\)\n\n5. **Calculate the total number of animals across all aquariums:**\n   - Total saltwater animals + Total freshwater animals = Total animals\n   - \\(285 + 1,178 = 1,463\\)\n\nTherefore, he has a total of 1,463 animals across all his aquariums."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the situation:**\n   - Dan has $3 left after buying a candy bar.\n   - The candy bar costs $2.\n\n2. **Determine the initial amount of money Dan had:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the initial amount of money Dan had.\n   - After buying the candy bar for $2, Dan has $3 left.\n\n3. **Set up the equation:**\n   - The equation based on the situation is: \n     \\[\n     x - 2 = 3\n     \\]\n   - This equation represents the initial amount of money minus the cost of the candy bar, which equals the amount of money Dan has left.\n\n4. **Solve the equation:**\n   - Add 2 to both sides of the equation to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x - 2 + 2 = 3 + 2\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     x = 5\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Dan initially had $5 before buying the candy bar.\n\nTherefore, Dan had $5 initially."

'To solve the problem of determining how many snakes were not hiding in the cage, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the total number of snakes in the cage:**\n   - Total number of snakes = 95\n\n2. **Identify the number of snakes that were hiding:**\n   - Number of snakes hiding = 64\n\n3. **Calculate the number of snakes that were not hiding:**\n   - Number of snakes not hiding = Total number of snakes - Number of snakes hiding\n   - Number of snakes not hiding = 95 - 64\n\n4. **Perform the subtraction:**\n   - 95 - 64 = 31\n\nTherefore, the number of snakes that were not hiding in the cage is 31.'
'To solve the problem of determining how many beads each necklace needed, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Emily made a total of 6 necklaces.\n   - She used a total of 18 beads for all the necklaces.\n\n2. **Determine the Number of Beads per Necklace:**\n   - We need to find out how many beads were used for each necklace.\n   - To do this, we divide the total number of beads by the total number of necklaces.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Total beads = 18\n   - Total necklaces = 6\n   - Beads per necklace = Total beads ÷ Total necklaces\n   - Beads per necklace = 18 ÷ 6\n\n4. **Calculate the Result:**\n   - Beads per necklace = 3\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each necklace needed 3 beads.\n\nTherefore, each necklace required 3 beads.'
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Bags of Cans on Monday:**\n   - Tiffany had 3 bags of cans.\n\n2. **Additional Bags of Cans Found the Next Day:**\n   - She found 7 more bags of cans.\n\n3. **Total Bags of Cans:**\n   - To find the total number of bags of cans Tiffany had, we need to add the bags she initially had to the bags she found the next day.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total bags of cans} = \\text{Initial bags of cans} + \\text{Additional bags of cans}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total bags of cans} = 3 + 7 = 10\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, Tiffany had a total of 10 bags of cans altogether."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Each package contains 7 pieces of gum.\n   - Robin has 6 extra pieces of gum.\n   - The total number of pieces of gum Robin has is 41.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of packages Robin has.\n   - The total number of pieces of gum from the packages is \\( 7x \\) (since each package has 7 pieces).\n   - Robin also has 6 extra pieces of gum.\n   - The total number of pieces of gum is 41.\n\n3. **Formulate the Equation:**\n   \\[\n   7x + 6 = 41\n   \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Subtract 6 from both sides to isolate the term with \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     7x = 41 - 6\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     7x = 35\n     \\]\n   - Divide both sides by 7 to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{35}{7}\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     x = 5\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Robin has 5 packages of gum.\n\nTherefore, Robin has 5 packages of gum."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Baker made a total of 155 cakes.\n   - His friend bought 140 cakes from him.\n\n2. **Determine How Many Cakes Are Left:**\n   - Start with the total number of cakes the baker made: 155 cakes.\n   - Subtract the number of cakes his friend bought: 140 cakes.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   155 \\text{ cakes} - 140 \\text{ cakes} = 15 \\text{ cakes}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - The baker has 15 cakes left after his friend bought 140 cakes from him.\n\nTherefore, the baker would still have 15 cakes."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Initial Number of Children on the Bus:**\n   - There were initially 2 children on the bus.\n\n2. **Total Number of Children After the Bus Stop:**\n   - After the bus stop, there were 10 children on the bus.\n\n3. **Determine How Many More Children Got on the Bus:**\n   - To find out how many more children got on the bus at the bus stop, we need to subtract the initial number of children from the total number of children after the bus stop.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of children who got on the bus} = \\text{Total children after the bus stop} - \\text{Initial children on the bus}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of children who got on the bus} = 10 - 2 = 8\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, 8 more children got on the bus at the bus stop."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Information Given:**\n   - Danny found 22 bottle caps at the park.\n   - After finding these bottle caps, Danny has a total of 28 bottle caps in his collection.\n\n2. **Objective:**\n   - Determine how many bottle caps Danny had in his collection before he went to the park.\n\n3. **Calculation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of bottle caps Danny had initially.\n   - After finding 22 bottle caps, his total became 28.\n   - Therefore, we can set up the equation: \n     \\[\n     x + 22 = 28\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Subtract 22 from both sides to find \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 28 - 22\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the result:\n     \\[\n     x = 6\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Danny initially had 6 bottle caps in his collection before he went to the park.\n\nTherefore, Danny had 6 bottle caps at first."

Therefore, we can write the equation:\n     \\[\n     B = 635 + 510\n     \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the number of boys:**\n   - Add the number of girls and the additional boys:\n     \\[\n     B = 635 + 510 = 1145\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - There are 1145 boys in the school.\n\nTherefore, the number of boys in the school is 1145."
"To solve the problem of determining how much longer Jesse's room is than it is wide, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the Length and Width:**\n   - Length of the room = 12 feet\n   - Width of the room = 11 feet\n\n2. **Calculate the Difference:**\n   - To find out how much longer the room is than it is wide, subtract the width from the length.\n   - Difference = Length - Width\n   - Difference = 12 feet - 11 feet\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Difference = 1 foot\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Jesse's room is 1 foot longer than it is wide.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Jesse's room is 1 foot longer than it is wide."

"To solve the problem, we need to determine how many seeds were planted in each flowerbed. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Total number of flowerbeds: 8\n   - Total number of seeds planted: 32\n   - Seeds are distributed equally among the flowerbeds.\n\n2. **Set Up the Problem:**\n   - We need to find out how many seeds are in each flowerbed. This can be done by dividing the total number of seeds by the total number of flowerbeds.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Divide the total number of seeds by the total number of flowerbeds:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Seeds per flowerbed} = \\frac{\\text{Total seeds}}{\\text{Total flowerbeds}} = \\frac{32}{8}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Calculate:**\n   - \\(\\frac{32}{8} = 4\\)\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Paige and her mom planted 4 seeds in each flowerbed.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that they planted 4 seeds in each flowerbed."

Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the number of school buses:**\n   - There are 95 school buses.\n\n2. **Identify the number of seats on each school bus:**\n   - Each school bus has 118 seats.\n\n3. **Determine if the buses are fully filled:**\n   - All school buses are fully filled.\n\n4. **Calculate the total number of students:**\n   - Since each bus is fully filled, the total number of students is the product of the number of buses and the number of seats per bus.\n   - Total number of students = Number of buses × Number of seats per bus\n   - Total number of students = 95 buses × 118 seats/bus\n\n5. **Perform the multiplication:**\n   - Total number of students = 95 × 118\n   - Total number of students = 11,210\n\nTherefore, the total number of students in the school is 11,210."

'To solve the problem of determining how many groups of size 2 can be formed from 18 bananas, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Total number of bananas: 18\n   - Size of each group: 2\n   - We need to find out how many groups of size 2 can be formed.\n\n2. **Set Up the Calculation:**\n   - To find the number of groups, we divide the total number of bananas by the size of each group.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of groups} = \\frac{\\text{Total number of bananas}}{\\text{Size of each group}} = \\frac{18}{2}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate:**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{18}{2} = 9\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - There are 9 groups of size 2 that can be formed from 18 bananas.\n\nTherefore, the answer is 9 groups.'

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the given information:**\n   - Rachel had to complete 8 pages of math homework.\n   - The number of math pages was 3 more than the number of reading pages.\n\n2. **Define the variables:**\n   - Let \\( R \\) represent the number of reading pages Rachel had to complete.\n\n3. **Set up the equation based on the relationship:**\n   - Since the number of math pages is 3 more than the number of reading pages, we can write the equation:\n     \\[\n     8 = R + 3\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the equation for \\( R \\):**\n   - Subtract 3 from both sides to find the number of reading pages:\n     \\[\n     R = 8 - 3\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     R = 5\n     \\]\n\n5. **Calculate the total number of pages:**\n   - Add the number of math pages and reading pages to find the total:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total pages} = \\text{Math pages} + \\text{Reading pages} = 8 + 5\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total pages} = 13\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, Rachel had to complete a total of 13 pages of homework."

'To solve the problem of determining how many kids Julia played with on Tuesday and Wednesday combined, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the number of kids Julia played with on each day:**\n   - On Tuesday, Julia played with 14 kids.\n   - On Wednesday, Julia played with 16 kids.\n\n2. **Add the number of kids from Tuesday and Wednesday:**\n   - Tuesday: 14 kids\n   - Wednesday: 16 kids\n\n3. **Perform the addition:**\n   \\[\n   14 \\text{ (Tuesday)} + 16 \\text{ (Wednesday)} = 30 \\text{ kids}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   Julia played with a total of 30 kids on Tuesday and Wednesday combined.\n\nTherefore, the answer is 30 kids.'

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Weekly Earnings:**\n   - Lewis earns $403 every week.\n\n2. **Duration of Harvest Season:**\n   - The harvest season lasts for 233 weeks.\n\n3. **Weekly Rent:**\n   - Lewis has to pay $49 rent every week.\n\nNow, let's calculate the total earnings and expenses over the 233 weeks:\n\n### Step 1: Calculate Total Earnings\n- Lewis earns $403 per week.\n- Total earnings over 233 weeks = \\( 403 \\times 233 \\).\n\n\\[ 403 \\times 233 = 93,899 \\]\n\nSo, Lewis earns a total of $93,899 over the 233 weeks.\n\n### Step 2: Calculate Total Rent Paid\n- Lewis pays $49 rent per week.\n- Total rent paid over 233 weeks = \\( 49 \\times 233 \\).\n\n\\[ 49 \\times 233 = 11,417 \\]\n\nSo, Lewis pays a total of $11,417 in rent over the 233 weeks.\n\n### Step 3: Calculate Net Earnings After Rent\n- Net earnings = Total earnings - Total rent paid.\n\n\\[ 93,899 - 11,417 = 82,482 \\]\n\nTherefore, after paying rent, Lewis earns a total of $82,482 during the 233 weeks of the harvest season."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - They harvest 16 sacks of oranges per day.\n   - The goal is to harvest 80 sacks of oranges.\n\n2. **Determine the Number of Days Needed:**\n   - We need to find out how many days it will take to harvest 80 sacks if 16 sacks are harvested each day.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - To find the number of days required, divide the total number of sacks needed by the number of sacks harvested per day.\n   - Calculation: \\( \\frac{80 \\text{ sacks}}{16 \\text{ sacks/day}} = 5 \\text{ days} \\).\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - It will take 5 days to harvest 80 sacks of oranges.\n\nTherefore, the answer is 5 days."
'To solve the problem of determining how many packages of gum Robin has, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Each package contains 3 pieces of gum.\n   - There is a total of 42 pieces of gum.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) represent the number of packages.\n   - Since each package contains 3 pieces of gum, the total number of pieces can be expressed as \\( 3x \\).\n\n3. **Use the Total Number of Pieces:**\n   - We know the total number of pieces of gum is 42. Therefore, we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     3x = 42\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve for \\( x \\):**\n   - To find \\( x \\), divide both sides of the equation by 3:\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{42}{3}\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the division:\n     \\[\n     x = 14\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Robin has 14 packages of gum.\n\nBy following these steps, we have determined that Robin has 14 packages of gum.'

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the given information:**\n   - The width of Jesse's room is 7 feet.\n   - The area of the carpet needed is 14 square feet.\n\n2. **Identify what needs to be found:**\n   - We need to find the length of Jesse's room.\n\n3. **Use the formula for the area of a rectangle:**\n   - The area of a rectangle is given by the formula: \n     \\[\n     \\text{Area} = \\text{Length} \\times \\text{Width}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Substitute the known values into the formula:**\n   - We know the area is 14 square feet and the width is 7 feet. So, we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     14 = \\text{Length} \\times 7\n     \\]\n\n5. **Solve for the length:**\n   - To find the length, divide both sides of the equation by 7:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Length} = \\frac{14}{7} = 2 \\text{ feet}\n     \\]\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - The length of Jesse's room is 2 feet.\n\nTherefore, the length of Jesse's room is 2 feet."

'To solve the problem of determining the total cost of buying 33 packs of DVDs, where each pack costs 81 dollars, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the cost per pack:**\n   - Each pack costs 81 dollars.\n\n2. **Identify the number of packs to be purchased:**\n   - The number of packs is 33.\n\n3. **Calculate the total cost:**\n   - Multiply the cost per pack by the number of packs to find the total cost.\n   - Total cost = Cost per pack × Number of packs\n   - Total cost = 81 dollars/pack × 33 packs\n\n4. **Perform the multiplication:**\n   - 81 × 33 = 2673\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The total cost to buy 33 packs of DVDs is 2673 dollars.\n\nTherefore, it will cost 2673 dollars to buy 33 packs of DVDs.'

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Harvesting and Discarding:**\n   - They harvest 74 sacks of oranges per day.\n   - They discard 71 sacks of oranges per day.\n\n2. **Net Sacks per Day:**\n   - To find out how many sacks they keep each day, subtract the number of sacks discarded from the number of sacks harvested:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Net sacks per day} = 74 - 71 = 3 \\text{ sacks}\n     \\]\n\n3. **Duration of Harvest:**\n   - The harvest lasts for 51 days.\n\n4. **Total Sacks After 51 Days:**\n   - Multiply the net sacks per day by the number of days to find the total number of sacks they will have after 51 days:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total sacks after 51 days} = 3 \\times 51 = 153 \\text{ sacks}\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, after 51 days of harvest, they will have 153 sacks of oranges."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Total Crackers**: Matthew had a total of 36 crackers.\n\n2. **Crackers per Friend**: He gave 6 crackers to each friend.\n\n3. **Objective**: We need to find out how many friends Matthew gave crackers to.\n\n### Steps to Solve:\n\n- **Step 1**: Identify the total number of crackers Matthew had.\n  - Total crackers = 36\n\n- **Step 2**: Identify how many crackers each friend received.\n  - Crackers per friend = 6\n\n- **Step 3**: Use division to find out how many friends received crackers.\n  - Number of friends = Total crackers ÷ Crackers per friend\n  - Number of friends = 36 ÷ 6\n\n- **Step 4**: Perform the division.\n  - Number of friends = 6\n\n### Conclusion:\n\nMatthew gave crackers to 6 friends."

Let's list the information and solve the problem step by step:\n\n- Today: 92 visitors\n- Yesterday: 419 visitors\n- Two days ago: 103 visitors\n- Three days ago: Unknown (this is what we need to find)\n\nSince we are given the number of visitors for today, yesterday, and two days ago, but not for three days ago, we cannot directly calculate the number of visitors for four days ago without additional information. The problem does not provide any further data or pattern to deduce the number of visitors for four days ago.\n\nTherefore, based on the information provided, we cannot determine the number of visitors who came to Buckingham Palace four days ago."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Number of visitors on the previous day:** 100\n2. **Number of visitors on that day:** 666\n\nWe need to find out how many more visitors visited the Buckingham Palace on that day compared to the previous day. To do this, we subtract the number of visitors on the previous day from the number of visitors on that day:\n\n\\[ \\text{Difference in visitors} = \\text{Number of visitors on that day} - \\text{Number of visitors on the previous day} \\]\n\n\\[ \\text{Difference in visitors} = 666 - 100 \\]\n\n\\[ \\text{Difference in visitors} = 566 \\]\n\nTherefore, 566 more visitors visited the Buckingham Palace on that day than on the previous day."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Number of Trees**: Rachel has 3 apple trees.\n\n2. **Apples Picked from Each Tree**: She picked 8 apples from each tree.\n\n3. **Total Apples Picked**: Since there are 3 trees and she picked 8 apples from each, the total number of apples picked is:\n   \\[\n   3 \\text{ trees} \\times 8 \\text{ apples/tree} = 24 \\text{ apples}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Apples Remaining on Trees**: After picking, there are 9 apples still on the trees.\n\n5. **Total Initial Apples**: To find the total number of apples initially on all the trees, we add the apples picked to the apples remaining:\n   \\[\n   24 \\text{ apples picked} + 9 \\text{ apples remaining} = 33 \\text{ apples}\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, there were initially 33 apples on all the trees."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Total number of students:** 92 students\n2. **Total number of school buses:** 46 buses\n3. **All buses are full.**\n\nWe need to find out how many seats are in each bus.\n\n**Step-by-step solution:**\n\n1. **Determine the total number of students per bus:**\n   - Since there are 92 students and 46 buses, and all buses are full, we divide the total number of students by the total number of buses to find out how many students are in each bus.\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of students per bus} = \\frac{92 \\text{ students}}{46 \\text{ buses}} = 2 \\text{ students per bus}\n   \\]\n\n2. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each bus has 2 seats, as each bus is full with 2 students.\n\nTherefore, there are 2 seats in each bus."
'To solve the problem of how much money Gwen received for her birthday, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Gwen spent 8 dollars.\n   - Gwen has 6 dollars left.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the total amount of money Gwen received for her birthday.\n   - According to the information, after spending 8 dollars, Gwen has 6 dollars left.\n\n3. **Formulate the Equation:**\n   - The equation based on the information is:\n     \\[\n     x - 8 = 6\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( x \\), add 8 to both sides of the equation:\n     \\[\n     x - 8 + 8 = 6 + 8\n     \\]\n   - Simplifying gives:\n     \\[\n     x = 14\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Gwen received 14 dollars for her birthday.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Gwen received 14 dollars for her birthday.'
'To solve the problem of determining how many bottle caps Danny initially had, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Danny lost 66 bottle caps at the park.\n   - Danny now has 25 bottle caps in his collection.\n\n2. **Determine What We Need to Find:**\n   - We need to find out how many bottle caps Danny had initially before he lost any.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of bottle caps Danny initially had.\n   - After losing 66 bottle caps, he has 25 left.\n   - This can be expressed as: \n     \\[\n     x - 66 = 25\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( x \\), add 66 to both sides of the equation:\n     \\[\n     x - 66 + 66 = 25 + 66\n     \\]\n   - Simplifying gives:\n     \\[\n     x = 91\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Danny initially had 91 bottle caps.\n\nTherefore, Danny had 91 bottle caps at first.'

'To determine how many chapters Frank read per day, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the total number of chapters in the book:**\n   - The book has 15 chapters.\n\n2. **Understand the total number of days Frank took to finish the book:**\n   - Frank took 660 days to finish the book.\n\n3. **Calculate the number of chapters Frank read per day:**\n   - To find out how many chapters Frank read per day, divide the total number of chapters by the total number of days.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Chapters per day} = \\frac{\\text{Total chapters}}{\\text{Total days}} = \\frac{15}{660}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the division:**\n\n   \\[\n   \\frac{15}{660} = \\frac{1}{44}\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Frank read \\(\\frac{1}{44}\\) of a chapter per day.\n\nTherefore, Frank read approximately 0.0227 chapters per day.'
"To solve the problem, let's break down the information given and solve it step by step.\n\n### Information Given:\n1. The grasshopper jumped 19 inches.\n2. The grasshopper jumped 4 inches farther than the frog.\n3. The mouse jumped 44 inches less than the frog.\n\n### Steps to Solve:\n\n1. **Determine the frog's jump distance:**\n   - Let \\( F \\) represent the distance the frog jumped in inches.\n   - According to the information, the grasshopper jumped 4 inches farther than the frog. Therefore, we can write the equation:\n     \\[\n     F + 4 = 19\n     \\]\n   - Solve for \\( F \\):\n     \\[\n     F = 19 - 4 = 15\n     \\]\n\n2. **Verify the mouse's jump distance:**\n   - The mouse jumped 44 inches less than the frog. Therefore, the mouse's jump distance is:\n     \\[\n     F - 44 = 15 - 44 = -29\n     \\]\n   - Since a negative jump distance doesn't make sense in this context, it indicates that the mouse's jump is not physically possible given the constraints. However, this doesn't affect the calculation of the frog's jump distance.\n\n### Conclusion:\nThe frog jumped 15 inches."
