"To solve the problem of how many inches of hair Robin cut off, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Robin's original hair length: 17 inches\n   - Robin's current hair length after cutting: 13 inches\n\n2. **Determine the Amount Cut:**\n   - To find out how much hair Robin cut off, subtract the current hair length from the original hair length.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Original hair length: 17 inches\n   - Current hair length: 13 inches\n   - Hair cut off = Original hair length - Current hair length\n   - Hair cut off = 17 inches - 13 inches\n\n4. **Calculate the Result:**\n   - Hair cut off = 4 inches\n\nTherefore, Robin cut off 4 inches of his hair."

'To solve the problem of determining how many school buses are needed for the field trip, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Calculate the Total Number of Students:**\n   - There are 67 classrooms.\n   - Each classroom has 66 students.\n   - Total number of students = 67 classrooms × 66 students/classroom = 4,422 students.\n\n2. **Determine the Capacity of Each Bus:**\n   - Each school bus has 6 seats.\n\n3. **Calculate the Number of Buses Needed:**\n   - To find out how many buses are needed, divide the total number of students by the number of seats per bus.\n   - Number of buses needed = Total number of students ÷ Seats per bus = 4,422 ÷ 6 = 737 buses.\n\nTherefore, 737 school buses are needed to transport all the students on the field trip.'
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - The Razorback t-shirt shop makes $87 off each t-shirt sold.\n   - They sold a total of 95 t-shirts during the Arkansas game and the Texas Tech game.\n   - They sold 47 t-shirts during the Arkansas game.\n\n2. **Calculate the Number of T-shirts Sold During the Texas Tech Game:**\n   - Total t-shirts sold = 95\n   - T-shirts sold during the Arkansas game = 47\n   - T-shirts sold during the Texas Tech game = Total t-shirts sold - T-shirts sold during the Arkansas game\n   - T-shirts sold during the Texas Tech game = 95 - 47 = 48\n\n3. **Calculate the Total Revenue:**\n   - Revenue from each t-shirt = $87\n   - Total t-shirts sold = 95\n   - Total revenue = Revenue from each t-shirt × Total t-shirts sold\n   - Total revenue = $87 × 95\n\n4. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Total revenue = $87 × 95 = $8,265\n\nTherefore, the Razorback t-shirt shop made $8,265 from selling the 95 t-shirts."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Total number of students:** 98 students\n2. **Total number of school buses:** 7 buses\n3. **All buses are full.**\n\nWe need to find out how many seats are in each bus if all 7 buses are full with the 98 students.\n\n**Step-by-step solution:**\n\n1. **Determine the total number of students:**  \n   - There are 98 students in total.\n\n2. **Determine the total number of buses:**  \n   - There are 7 buses.\n\n3. **Calculate the number of students per bus:**  \n   - Since all buses are full and there are 98 students distributed equally among 7 buses, we divide the total number of students by the total number of buses to find the number of students per bus.\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of students per bus} = \\frac{98 \\text{ students}}{7 \\text{ buses}} = 14 \\text{ students per bus}\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, each bus has 14 seats to accommodate the students."
"To solve the problem, we need to determine the total number of blocks Randy used to build both the tower and the house. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the number of blocks used for each structure:**\n   - Randy uses 27 blocks to build a tower.\n   - Randy uses 53 blocks to build a house.\n\n2. **Calculate the total number of blocks used:**\n   - Add the number of blocks used for the tower and the house together.\n   - Total blocks used = Blocks for the tower + Blocks for the house\n   - Total blocks used = 27 + 53\n\n3. **Perform the addition:**\n   - 27 + 53 = 80\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Randy used a total of 80 blocks to build both the tower and the house.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Randy used 80 blocks in total to build the tower and the house."

Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the profit from each item:**\n   - Profit from each t-shirt: $86\n   - Profit from each jersey: $232\n\n2. **Calculate the difference in profit between a jersey and a t-shirt:**\n   - Difference = Profit from each jersey - Profit from each t-shirt\n   - Difference = $232 - $86\n\n3. **Perform the calculation:**\n   - Difference = $232 - $86 = $146\n\nTherefore, a jersey costs $146 more than a t-shirt based on the profit made from each item."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Information Given:**\n   - Danny found 66 wrappers at the park.\n   - Danny now has 68 wrappers in his collection.\n\n2. **Question:**\n   - How many wrappers did Danny have in his collection before he found the 66 wrappers at the park?\n\n3. **Step-by-Step Solution:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of wrappers Danny had initially.\n   - After finding 66 wrappers at the park, Danny's total number of wrappers became 68.\n   - Therefore, we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     x + 66 = 68\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Subtract 66 from both sides to find \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 68 - 66\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the right side:\n     \\[\n     x = 2\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Danny initially had 2 wrappers in his collection before he found the 66 wrappers at the park.\n\nTherefore, Danny had 2 wrappers at first."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Adam and Jackie together have 7 apples.\n   - He has 9 more apples than the combined total of Adam and Jackie's apples.\n\n2. **Translate the Information into an Equation:**\n   - Let \\( A \\) represent the number of apples Adam and Jackie have together. According to the problem, \\( A = 7 \\).\n   - Let \\( H \\) represent the number of apples He has.\n   - According to the problem, He has 9 more apples than Adam and Jackie together, so we can write the equation:  \n     \\[\n     H = A + 9\n     \\]\n\n3. **Substitute the Known Value:**\n   - Substitute \\( A = 7 \\) into the equation:  \n     \\[\n     H = 7 + 9\n     \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the Result:**\n   - Perform the addition:  \n     \\[\n     H = 16\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - He has 16 apples.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that He has 16 apples."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Count:**\n   - Dave initially had 11 apps on his phone.\n   - Dave initially had 3 files on his phone.\n\n2. **After Deletion:**\n   - Dave has 2 apps left.\n   - Dave has 24 files left.\n\n3. **Core Question:**\n   - We need to find out how many more files than apps Dave has left on his phone.\n\n4. **Calculation:**\n   - Number of files left = 24\n   - Number of apps left = 2\n   - Difference between files and apps = Number of files left - Number of apps left\n   - Difference = 24 - 2 = 22\n\nTherefore, Dave has 22 more files than apps left on his phone."
"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understanding the Problem:**\n   - Rebecca wants to split a collection of eggs into groups of 11.\n   - Each group contains 2 eggs.\n\n2. **Clarifying the Information:**\n   - The problem states that each group of 11 should contain 2 eggs. This seems contradictory because a group of 11 should logically contain 11 eggs, not 2. However, based on the information given, we will proceed with the understanding that each group is intended to have 2 eggs.\n\n3. **Calculating the Total Number of Eggs:**\n   - If each group is supposed to have 2 eggs, and she wants to form groups of 11, it implies that she is forming multiple groups, each with 2 eggs.\n   - Therefore, the total number of eggs Rebecca has is simply the number of eggs in each group multiplied by the number of groups.\n\n4. **Formulating the Calculation:**\n   - Since each group has 2 eggs, and she wants to form groups of 11, the total number of eggs is:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total number of eggs} = 2 \\times 11 = 22\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Rebecca has 22 eggs.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Rebecca has 22 eggs."

'To solve the problem of how much farther the frog jumped than the grasshopper, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - The frog jumped 39 inches.\n   - The grasshopper jumped 17 inches.\n\n2. **Identify What is Being Asked:**\n   - We need to find out how much farther the frog jumped compared to the grasshopper.\n\n3. **Set Up the Calculation:**\n   - To find out how much farther the frog jumped, subtract the distance the grasshopper jumped from the distance the frog jumped.\n\n4. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Distance the frog jumped} - \\text{Distance the grasshopper jumped} = 39 \\text{ inches} - 17 \\text{ inches} = 22 \\text{ inches}\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The frog jumped 22 inches farther than the grasshopper.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that the frog jumped 22 inches farther than the grasshopper.'

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the situation:**\n   - Rachel has 52 apple trees, but we are focusing on just one specific tree.\n   - She picked 2 apples from this tree.\n   - After picking, the tree still has 7 apples on it.\n\n2. **Determine the initial number of apples:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the initial number of apples on the tree.\n   - Rachel picked 2 apples, so the number of apples left on the tree is \\( x - 2 \\).\n   - We know that after picking, there are 7 apples left on the tree.\n\n3. **Set up the equation:**\n   \\[\n   x - 2 = 7\n   \\]\n\n4. **Solve the equation:**\n   - Add 2 to both sides of the equation to solve for \\( x \\):\n   \\[\n   x - 2 + 2 = 7 + 2\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x = 9\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The tree initially had 9 apples.\n\nTherefore, the tree had 9 apples to begin with."
"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and calculate the number of pizza slices each person gets:\n\n1. **Total number of pizzas**: 9  \n2. **Slices per pizza**: 10  \n\nFirst, calculate the total number of slices from all the pizzas:\n\n\\[ \\text{Total slices} = \\text{Total number of pizzas} \\times \\text{Slices per pizza} \\]\n\n\\[ \\text{Total slices} = 9 \\times 10 = 90 \\]\n\n3. **Total number of people**: 2  \n\nNext, distribute the total number of slices equally between the two people:\n\n\\[ \\text{Slices per person} = \\frac{\\text{Total slices}}{\\text{Total number of people}} \\]\n\n\\[ \\text{Slices per person} = \\frac{90}{2} = 45 \\]\n\nTherefore, each person gets 45 slices of pizza."

Therefore, we can write the equation:\n     \\[\n     3 \\, (\\text{hours on English}) + x \\, (\\text{hours on Chinese}) = 4 \\, (\\text{total hours})\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve the equation:**\n   - Subtract 3 from both sides of the equation to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 4 - 3\n     \\]\n   - Simplify the right side:\n     \\[\n     x = 1\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Ryan spends 1 hour on learning Chinese each day.\n\nTherefore, Ryan spends 1 hour on learning Chinese every day."

'To solve the problem of determining how many white t-shirts are in each package, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Given Information:**\n   - Total number of packages = 28\n   - Total number of white t-shirts = 56\n\n2. **Determine the Number of T-Shirts per Package:**\n   - We need to find out how many t-shirts are in each package. This can be done by dividing the total number of t-shirts by the total number of packages.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of t-shirts per package} = \\frac{\\text{Total number of t-shirts}}{\\text{Total number of packages}} = \\frac{56}{28}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the Result:**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{56}{28} = 2\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each package contains 2 white t-shirts.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that each package has 2 white t-shirts.'
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Identify the number of pastries and cakes made:**\n   - The baker made 52 pastries.\n   - The baker made 84 cakes.\n\n2. **Determine the difference between the number of cakes and pastries made:**\n   - To find out how many more cakes than pastries the baker made, subtract the number of pastries from the number of cakes.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Difference} = \\text{Number of cakes} - \\text{Number of pastries}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Difference} = 84 - 52\n   \\]\n\n3. **Calculate the difference:**\n   - Perform the subtraction:\n\n   \\[\n   84 - 52 = 32\n   \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - The baker made 32 more cakes than pastries.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that the baker made 32 more cakes than pastries."

So, the number of action figures becomes \\( x + 2 \\).\n\n3. **Removing Action Figures**: Jerry removed 7 of the old action figures. "To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Jessie lost 126 kilograms after she started jogging every day.\n   - Jessie currently weighs 66 kilograms.\n\n2. **Determine Jessie's Original Weight:**\n   - We need to find out how much Jessie weighed before she started jogging.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be Jessie's original weight before she started jogging.\n   - According to the information, after losing 126 kilograms, her weight is now 66 kilograms.\n   - This can be expressed as an equation:  \n     \\[\n     x - 126 = 66\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( x \\), add 126 to both sides of the equation:\n     \\[\n     x = 66 + 126\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the sum:\n     \\[\n     x = 192\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Jessie weighed 192 kilograms before she started jogging.\n\nTherefore, Jessie weighed 192 kilograms before she started jogging."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the number of marbles lost and found:**\n   - Josh lost 8 marbles.\n   - Josh found 10 new marbles.\n\n2. **Determine how many more marbles Josh found than he lost:**\n   - To find out how many more marbles Josh found than he lost, subtract the number of marbles lost from the number of marbles found.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Marbles found} - \\text{Marbles lost} = 10 - 8\n   \\]\n\n3. **Calculate the result:**\n   - \\(10 - 8 = 2\\)\n\nTherefore, Josh found 2 more marbles than he lost."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Original Number of Cards:**\n   - Nell originally had 239 baseball cards.\n   - Nell originally had 38 Ace cards.\n\n2. **Cards After Giving Some to Jeff:**\n   - Nell now has 111 baseball cards left.\n   - Nell now has 376 Ace cards left.\n\n3. **Core Question:**\n   - We need to find out how many more Ace cards than baseball cards Nell has after giving some cards to Jeff.\n\n4. **Calculation:**\n   - Number of Ace cards Nell has now: 376\n   - Number of baseball cards Nell has now: 111\n\n5. **Difference Calculation:**\n   - Difference in the number of Ace cards and baseball cards = Number of Ace cards - Number of baseball cards\n   - Difference = 376 - 111 = 265\n\nTherefore, Nell has 265 more Ace cards than baseball cards after giving some cards to Jeff."

"To solve the problem, we need to determine how many crayons Paul originally received for his birthday. We know two key pieces of information:\n\n1. Paul lost or gave away 551 crayons.\n2. Paul had 177 crayons left at the end of the school year.\n\nLet's break down the problem step by step:\n\n1. **Define the variables:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the total number of crayons Paul received for his birthday.\n\n2. **Set up the equation:**\n   - The total number of crayons Paul started with minus the crayons he lost or gave away should equal the number of crayons he has left.\n   - Therefore, the equation is: \n     \\[\n     x - 551 = 177\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve the equation:**\n   - Add 551 to both sides of the equation to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 177 + 551\n     \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the total:**\n   - Perform the addition:\n     \\[\n     x = 728\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, Paul received 728 crayons for his birthday."
"To solve the problem, we need to determine how many bookshelves Bryan has if he has a total of 42 books and each bookshelf contains 2 books. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Total number of books Bryan has: 42\n   - Number of books each bookshelf can hold: 2\n\n2. **Set Up the Calculation:**\n   - To find the number of bookshelves, we need to divide the total number of books by the number of books each bookshelf can hold.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of bookshelves} = \\frac{\\text{Total number of books}}{\\text{Number of books per bookshelf}} = \\frac{42}{2}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate:**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{42}{2} = 21\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Bryan has 21 bookshelves.\n\nTherefore, Bryan has 21 bookshelves."

Therefore, the equation is:\n     \\[\n     x + 12 = 16\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Subtract 12 from both sides to find \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 16 - 12\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the right side:\n     \\[\n     x = 4\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Julia played tag with 4 kids on Tuesday.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Julia played with 4 kids on Tuesday."

"To solve the problem, we need to calculate the total amount of money made by the ring toss game over the 22 days at the carnival. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the daily earnings:**\n   - The ring toss game made $144 per day.\n\n2. **Identify the number of days:**\n   - They were at the carnival for 22 days.\n\n3. **Calculate the total earnings:**\n   - To find the total earnings, multiply the daily earnings by the number of days:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total earnings} = \\text{Daily earnings} \\times \\text{Number of days}\n     \\]\n   - Plug in the values:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total earnings} = 144 \\times 22\n     \\]\n\n4. **Perform the multiplication:**\n   - Calculate \\(144 \\times 22\\):\n     \\[\n     144 \\times 22 = 3168\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The ring toss game made a total of $3,168 over the 22 days at the carnival.\n\nTherefore, the total amount of money made by the ring toss game is $3,168."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Composition of One Basket:**\n   - Each basket contains 19 red peaches.\n   - Each basket contains 4 green peaches.\n\n2. **Calculate the Total Number of Peaches in One Basket:**\n   - Total peaches in one basket = Number of red peaches + Number of green peaches\n   - Total peaches in one basket = 19 red peaches + 4 green peaches = 23 peaches\n\n3. **Determine the Number of Baskets:**\n   - There are 15 baskets in total.\n\n4. **Calculate the Total Number of Peaches in All Baskets:**\n   - Total peaches in all baskets = Total peaches in one basket × Number of baskets\n   - Total peaches in all baskets = 23 peaches/basket × 15 baskets = 345 peaches\n\nTherefore, there are a total of 345 peaches in the 15 baskets."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Jake has 17 peaches.\n   - Jake has 11 fewer peaches than Steven.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( S \\) represent the number of peaches Steven has.\n   - According to the problem, Jake has 11 fewer peaches than Steven, which can be expressed as:\n     \\[\n     J = S - 11\n     \\]\n   - We know from the problem that Jake has 17 peaches, so:\n     \\[\n     J = 17\n     \\]\n\n3. **Substitute and Solve:**\n   - Substitute \\( J = 17 \\) into the equation:\n     \\[\n     17 = S - 11\n     \\]\n   - To find \\( S \\), add 11 to both sides of the equation:\n     \\[\n     17 + 11 = S\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     S = 28\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Steven has 28 peaches.\n\nTherefore, Steven has 28 peaches."

'To solve the problem of determining how many bananas are in each group when 203 bananas are organized into 7 groups, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the Total Number of Bananas:**\n   - Total bananas = 203\n\n2. **Identify the Number of Groups:**\n   - Number of groups = 7\n\n3. **Calculate the Number of Bananas per Group:**\n   - To find out how many bananas are in each group, divide the total number of bananas by the number of groups.\n   - Calculation: \\( \\frac{203}{7} \\)\n\n4. **Perform the Division:**\n   - \\( 203 \\div 7 = 29 \\)\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each group contains 29 bananas.\n\nTherefore, when 203 bananas are organized into 7 groups, each group contains 29 bananas.'

"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Define Variables:**\n   - Let \\( A \\) represent the number of apples Adam has.\n   - Let \\( J \\) represent the number of apples Jackie has.\n   - Let \\( H \\) represent the number of apples He has.\n\n2. **Translate the Information into Equations:**\n   - From the first hint: Together, Adam and Jackie have 12 apples.\n     \\[\n     A + J = 12\n     \\]\n   - From the second hint: He has 9 apples more than Adam and Jackie together do.\n     \\[\n     H = (A + J) + 9\n     \\]\n   - From the third hint: Adam has 8 more apples than Jackie.\n     \\[\n     A = J + 8\n     \\]\n\n3. **Substitute and Solve:**\n   - Substitute the expression for \\( A \\) from the third equation into the first equation:\n     \\[\n     (J + 8) + J = 12\n     \\]\n   - Simplify and solve for \\( J \\):\n     \\[\n     2J + 8 = 12\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     2J = 4\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     J = 2\n     \\]\n\n4. **Find \\( A \\):**\n   - Substitute \\( J = 2 \\) back into the equation for \\( A \\):\n     \\[\n     A = J + 8 = 2 + 8 = 10\n     \\]\n\n5. **Find \\( H \\):**\n   - Substitute \\( A = 10 \\) and \\( J = 2 \\) into the equation for \\( H \\):\n     \\[\n     H = (A + J) + 9 = (10 + 2) + 9 = 12 + 9 = 21\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, He has 21 apples."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Amount in Wallet:**\n   - Olivia initially had $106 in her wallet.\n\n2. **Amount Left After Shopping:**\n   - After visiting both the supermarket and the showroom, Olivia had $26 left.\n\n3. **Amount Spent at the Showroom:**\n   - Olivia spent $49 at the showroom.\n\nNow, we need to find out how much Olivia spent at the supermarket.\n\n**Step-by-Step Calculation:**\n\n1. **Calculate Total Amount Spent:**\n   - To find out how much Olivia spent in total, subtract the amount left from the initial amount:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total Amount Spent} = \\text{Initial Amount} - \\text{Amount Left}\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total Amount Spent} = 106 - 26 = 80\n     \\]\n\n2. **Calculate Amount Spent at the Supermarket:**\n   - Since we know the total amount spent and the amount spent at the showroom, we can find the amount spent at the supermarket by subtracting the showroom expenditure from the total expenditure:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Amount Spent at Supermarket} = \\text{Total Amount Spent} - \\text{Amount Spent at Showroom}\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     \\text{Amount Spent at Supermarket} = 80 - 49 = 31\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, Olivia spent $31 at the supermarket."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Grasshopper's Jump:**\n   - The grasshopper jumped 24 inches.\n\n2. **Frog's Jump:**\n   - The frog jumped 33 inches farther than the grasshopper.\n   - Therefore, the frog's jump = Grasshopper's jump + 33 inches = 24 inches + 33 inches = 57 inches.\n\n3. **Mouse's Jump:**\n   - The mouse jumped 5 inches less than the frog.\n   - Therefore, the mouse's jump = Frog's jump - 5 inches = 57 inches - 5 inches = 52 inches.\n\n4. **Difference between Mouse's and Grasshopper's Jumps:**\n   - To find out how much farther the mouse jumped than the grasshopper, subtract the grasshopper's jump from the mouse's jump.\n   - Difference = Mouse's jump - Grasshopper's jump = 52 inches - 24 inches = 28 inches.\n\nTherefore, the mouse jumped 28 inches farther than the grasshopper."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Current Situation:**\n   - After Rachel picked apples, the tree has:\n     - 2 ripe apples\n     - 4 unripe apples\n\n2. **Determine the Number of Ripe Apples Before Picking:**\n   - Rachel picked 6 ripe apples.\n   - After picking, there are 2 ripe apples left on the tree.\n   - Therefore, before picking, the tree had:\n     \\[\n     6 \\text{ (picked ripe apples)} + 2 \\text{ (remaining ripe apples)} = 8 \\text{ ripe apples}\n     \\]\n\n3. **Determine the Total Number of Apples Before Picking:**\n   - After picking, the tree has a total of:\n     \\[\n     2 \\text{ (ripe apples)} + 4 \\text{ (unripe apples)} = 6 \\text{ apples}\n     \\]\n   - Before picking, the tree had:\n     \\[\n     8 \\text{ (ripe apples)} + 4 \\text{ (unripe apples)} = 12 \\text{ apples}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - The tree originally had 12 apples before Rachel picked any.\n\nTherefore, the tree had 12 apples to begin with."
'To solve the problem of how many days Frank took to finish reading a 392-page book at a rate of 14 pages per day, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the total number of pages in the book:**\n   - Total pages = 392\n\n2. **Identify the number of pages Frank reads per day:**\n   - Pages per day = 14\n\n3. **Calculate the number of days Frank took to finish the book:**\n   - To find the number of days, divide the total number of pages by the number of pages read per day.\n   - Days = Total pages / Pages per day\n   - Days = 392 / 14\n\n4. **Perform the division:**\n   - 392 ÷ 14 = 28\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Frank took 28 days to finish reading the book.\n\nTherefore, Frank took 28 days to finish reading the 392-page book.'
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Situation:**\n   - Let \\( D \\) be the initial number of marbles Doug had.\n   - Ed had 24 more marbles than Doug, so Ed had \\( D + 24 \\) marbles.\n\n2. **Changes in the Number of Marbles:**\n   - Doug lost 27 marbles, so now Doug has \\( D - 27 \\) marbles.\n   - Ed found 9 more marbles, so now Ed has \\( (D + 24) + 9 = D + 33 \\) marbles.\n\n3. **Calculate the Difference:**\n   - We need to find out how many more marbles Ed has than Doug after these changes.\n   - The difference in the number of marbles between Ed and Doug is:\n     \\[\n     (D + 33) - (D - 27) = D + 33 - D + 27 = 33 + 27 = 60\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, after Doug lost 27 marbles and Ed found 9 more marbles, Ed had 60 more marbles than Doug."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Faye has 35 pencils.\n   - She is placing the pencils into rows with 5 pencils in each row.\n\n2. **Determine the Number of Rows:**\n   - To find out how many rows Faye can make, we need to divide the total number of pencils by the number of pencils per row.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Total number of pencils = 35\n   - Number of pencils per row = 5\n   - Number of rows = Total number of pencils ÷ Number of pencils per row\n   - Number of rows = 35 ÷ 5\n\n4. **Calculate:**\n   - 35 ÷ 5 = 7\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Faye can make 7 rows of pencils with 5 pencils in each row.\n\nTherefore, Faye can make 7 rows."
"To solve the problem, let's follow the hints and break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Initially, there were some children on the bus.\n   - At the bus stop, 2 more children got on the bus.\n   - After these 2 children got on, there were 41 children in total on the bus.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of children on the bus before the bus stop.\n   - After 2 more children got on, the total number of children on the bus became 41.\n\n3. **Formulate the Equation:**\n   - The equation based on the information given is:\n     \\[\n     x + 2 = 41\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Subtract 2 from both sides to find \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 41 - 2\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the result:\n     \\[\n     x = 39\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - There were 39 children riding on the bus before the bus stop.\n\nTherefore, the number of children on the bus before the bus stop was 39."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided in the hint:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - The mailman gives 2 junk mails to each house.\n   - The total number of junk mails to be delivered to the block is 14.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of houses in the block.\n   - Since each house receives 2 junk mails, the total number of junk mails delivered is \\( 2 \\times x \\).\n\n3. **Use the Total Number of Junk Mails:**\n   - According to the problem, the total number of junk mails is 14.\n   - Therefore, we can set up the equation: \n     \\[\n     2 \\times x = 14\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve for \\( x \\):**\n   - Divide both sides of the equation by 2 to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{14}{2} = 7\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - There are 7 houses in the block.\n\nTherefore, the number of houses in the block is 7."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the hints provided:\n\n1. **Understand the relationship between Ed and Doug's marbles:**\n   - Ed had 6 more marbles than Doug.\n   - Ed had 22 marbles.\n\n2. **Calculate how many marbles Doug originally had:**\n   - Since Ed had 6 more marbles than Doug, we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Doug's original marbles} = \\text{Ed's marbles} - 6\n     \\]\n   - Substitute the number of marbles Ed had:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Doug's original marbles} = 22 - 6 = 16\n     \\]\n\n3. **Account for the marbles Doug lost:**\n   - Doug lost 7 marbles at the playground.\n   - Therefore, the number of marbles Doug has now is:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Doug's current marbles} = \\text{Doug's original marbles} - 7\n     \\]\n   - Substitute the number of marbles Doug originally had:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Doug's current marbles} = 16 - 7 = 9\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Doug now has 9 marbles.\n\nTherefore, after losing 7 marbles, Doug has 9 marbles left."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the hints provided:\n\n1. **Initial Situation:**\n   - The waiter initially had 3 customers.\n\n2. **After Some Customers Left:**\n   - The waiter ended up with 4 customers remaining.\n\n3. **Understanding the Change:**\n   - Since the waiter has more customers remaining (4) than he initially had (3), it means new customers must have arrived.\n\n4. **Calculate the Number of New Customers:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of new customers who arrived.\n   - The equation based on the situation is: \n     \\[\n     \\text{Initial customers} - \\text{Customers who left} + \\text{New customers} = \\text{Remaining customers}\n     \\]\n   - Substituting the known values:\n     \\[\n     3 - (\\text{Customers who left}) + x = 4\n     \\]\n\n5. **Solve for the Number of Customers Who Left:**\n   - Rearrange the equation to find the number of customers who left:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Customers who left} = 3 + x - 4\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     \\text{Customers who left} = x - 1\n     \\]\n\n6. **Determine the Number of New Customers:**\n   - Since the remaining customers are 4, and initially there were 3, at least 1 new customer must have arrived to make the total 4.\n   - Therefore, \\( x = 1 \\).\n\n7. **Calculate the Number of Customers Who Left:**\n   - Substitute \\( x = 1 \\) into the equation for customers who left:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Customers who left} = 1 - 1 = 0\n     \\]\n\n8. **Calculate the Difference:**\n   - The number of customers who stayed behind is 4.\n   - The number of customers who left is 0.\n   - The difference is:\n     \\[\n     4 - 0 = 4\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, 4 more customers stayed behind than those that left."

'To solve the problem of determining how many sacks of oranges were harvested per day, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Total number of sacks harvested: 56 sacks\n   - Total number of days of harvesting: 14 days\n\n2. **Set Up the Calculation:**\n   - We need to find the number of sacks harvested per day. This can be calculated by dividing the total number of sacks by the total number of days.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Sacks per day} = \\frac{\\text{Total sacks}}{\\text{Total days}} = \\frac{56 \\text{ sacks}}{14 \\text{ days}}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Sacks per day} = 4 \\text{ sacks per day}\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - They harvested 4 sacks of oranges per day.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that they harvested 4 sacks of oranges per day.'
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the hints provided:\n\n1. **Define Variables:**\n   - Let \\( J \\) represent the number of apples Jackie has.\n   - Since Adam has 4 more apples than Jackie, Adam has \\( J + 4 \\) apples.\n\n2. **Equation for Adam and Jackie:**\n   - Together, Adam and Jackie have 14 apples. Therefore, we can write the equation:\n     \\[\n     J + (J + 4) = 14\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve for \\( J \\):**\n   - Simplify the equation:\n     \\[\n     2J + 4 = 14\n     \\]\n   - Subtract 4 from both sides:\n     \\[\n     2J = 10\n     \\]\n   - Divide by 2:\n     \\[\n     J = 5\n     \\]\n\n4. **Find the Number of Apples Adam Has:**\n   - Since Adam has 4 more apples than Jackie:\n     \\[\n     J + 4 = 5 + 4 = 9\n     \\]\n\n5. **Calculate the Total Number of Apples Adam and Jackie Have:**\n   - Verify the total:\n     \\[\n     J + (J + 4) = 5 + 9 = 14\n     \\]\n   - This confirms the total is correct.\n\n6. **Determine How Many Apples Bob Has:**\n   - Bob has 6 more apples than Adam and Jackie together:\n     \\[\n     14 + 6 = 20\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, Bob has 20 apples."
"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Recipe Requirements:**\n   - The recipe calls for 6 cups of flour.\n   - The recipe calls for 13 cups of sugar.\n\n2. **Understand the Current Situation:**\n   - Mary still needs 8 more cups of flour than sugar.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of cups of flour Mary has already added.\n   - According to the problem, Mary needs 8 more cups of flour than sugar. Therefore, the amount of flour she needs in total is the amount of sugar plus 8 cups.\n   - Since the recipe calls for 13 cups of sugar, the total amount of flour she needs is \\( 13 + 8 = 21 \\) cups.\n\n4. **Calculate the Additional Flour Needed:**\n   - Mary needs a total of 21 cups of flour.\n   - She has already added \\( x \\) cups of flour.\n   - Therefore, the additional flour she needs to add is \\( 21 - x \\).\n\n5. **Use the Recipe Requirement:**\n   - The recipe calls for 6 cups of flour, which means \\( x \\) must be less than or equal to 6 for her to still need more flour.\n   - However, since she needs 21 cups in total, the calculation of how much more she needs to add is independent of the initial 6 cups requirement because the problem states she needs 8 more cups of flour than sugar.\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - Mary needs to add \\( 21 - x \\) cups of flour.\n   - Since the problem does not specify how many cups of flour she has already added, we cannot determine the exact number of additional cups needed without that information. However, the total amount she needs to reach is 21 cups of flour.\n\nIf you have any specific value for \\( x \\), you can substitute it into the equation \\( 21 - x \\) to find the exact number of additional cups needed."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Initial Information:**\n   - Initially, there were 41 bird families living near the mountain.\n\n2. **Understand the Change:**\n   - 27 bird families flew away for the winter.\n\n3. **Calculate the Remaining Bird Families:**\n   - To find out how many bird families are left, subtract the number of bird families that flew away from the initial number of bird families.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Remaining bird families} = \\text{Initial bird families} - \\text{Bird families that flew away}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Remaining bird families} = 41 - 27\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Subtract 27 from 41:\n\n   \\[\n   41 - 27 = 14\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - There are 14 bird families left near the mountain.\n\nTherefore, the number of bird families left near the mountain is 14."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the hints provided:\n\n1. **Identify the number of peaches Jill has:**\n   - Jill has 12 peaches.\n\n2. **Determine the number of peaches Steven has:**\n   - Steven has 15 more peaches than Jill.\n   - Since Jill has 12 peaches, Steven has \\(12 + 15 = 27\\) peaches.\n\n3. **Determine the number of peaches Jake has:**\n   - Jake has 16 fewer peaches than Steven.\n   - Since Steven has 27 peaches, Jake has \\(27 - 16 = 11\\) peaches.\n\n4. **Calculate how many more peaches Jill has than Jake:**\n   - Jill has 12 peaches, and Jake has 11 peaches.\n   - The difference is \\(12 - 11 = 1\\).\n\nTherefore, Jill has 1 more peach than Jake."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - The first chapter is 60 pages long.\n   - The total number of pages in the book is 93.\n\n2. **Identify What We Need to Find:**\n   - We need to find the number of pages in the second chapter.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Total pages in the book = Pages in the first chapter + Pages in the second chapter\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of pages in the second chapter.\n   - Therefore, the equation is: \\( 60 + x = 93 \\)\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Subtract 60 from both sides to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 93 - 60\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the result:\n     \\[\n     x = 33\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The second chapter has 33 pages.\n\nTherefore, the second chapter contains 33 pages."
'To find out how many crayons Paul received for his birthday, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the crayons Paul gave away and lost:**\n   - Paul gave 563 crayons to his friends.\n   - Paul lost 558 crayons.\n\n2. **Identify the crayons Paul has left:**\n   - Paul has 332 crayons left.\n\n3. **Set up the equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of crayons Paul received for his birthday.\n   - The total number of crayons Paul had initially is equal to the number of crayons he gave away, plus the number of crayons he lost, plus the number of crayons he has left.\n\n4. **Write the equation:**\n   \\[\n   x = 563 + 558 + 332\n   \\]\n\n5. **Calculate the total:**\n   \\[\n   x = 563 + 558 + 332 = 1453\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, Paul received 1,453 crayons for his birthday.'
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Initial Number of People on the Bus:**\n   - There were initially 4 people on the bus.\n\n2. **Number of People Getting On at the Stop:**\n   - At the stop, 13 more people got on the bus.\n\n3. **Total Number of People on the Bus Now:**\n   - To find the total number of people on the bus now, add the initial number of people to the number of people who got on at the stop.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total number of people on the bus} = \\text{Initial number of people} + \\text{Number of people who got on}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total number of people on the bus} = 4 + 13\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total number of people on the bus} = 17\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, there are 17 people on the bus now."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Total Number of Kids**: Julia played with a total of 16 kids over two days (Monday and Tuesday).\n\n2. **Kids on Tuesday**: Julia played with 14 kids on Tuesday.\n\n3. **Kids on Monday**: We need to find out how many kids Julia played with on Monday.\n\nNow, let's calculate the number of kids she played with on Monday:\n\n- Since the total number of kids she played with over the two days is 16, and she played with 14 kids on Tuesday, we can find the number of kids she played with on Monday by subtracting the number of kids she played with on Tuesday from the total number of kids.\n\n\\[ \\text{Kids on Monday} = \\text{Total Kids} - \\text{Kids on Tuesday} \\]\n\n\\[ \\text{Kids on Monday} = 16 - 14 \\]\n\n\\[ \\text{Kids on Monday} = 2 \\]\n\nTherefore, Julia played with 2 kids on Monday."
'To solve the problem of determining how many cakes the baker still has after selling some to his friend, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Initial Number of Cakes**: The baker initially made 169 cakes.\n\n2. **Number of Cakes Sold**: The baker sold 137 cakes to his friend.\n\n3. **Calculate Remaining Cakes**: To find out how many cakes the baker still has, subtract the number of cakes sold from the initial number of cakes.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Remaining Cakes} = \\text{Initial Number of Cakes} - \\text{Number of Cakes Sold}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Remaining Cakes} = 169 - 137\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the Calculation**:\n\n   \\[\n   169 - 137 = 32\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the baker still has 32 cakes left after selling 137 cakes to his friend.'

"To determine how much money Lewis earns each week, we need to divide his total earnings by the number of weeks he worked. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Total earnings over 19 weeks**: $133\n2. **Total number of weeks**: 19 weeks\n3. **Core question**: How much money does Lewis earn each week?\n\nNow, let's calculate:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Earnings per week} = \\frac{\\text{Total earnings}}{\\text{Total number of weeks}} = \\frac{133}{19}\n\\]\n\nPerform the division:\n\n\\[\n133 \\div 19 = 7\n\\]\n\nTherefore, Lewis earns $7 each week.\n\n**Answer**: Lewis earns $7 each week."
'To solve the problem of finding out how many books Paul had initially before selling 137 at the garage sale, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Paul sold 137 books in a garage sale.\n   - After selling, he had 105 books left.\n\n2. **Identify What We Need to Find:**\n   - We need to find out how many books Paul had initially before selling any.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of books Paul had initially.\n   - After selling 137 books, he had 105 books left.\n   - This can be expressed as: \n     \\[\n     x - 137 = 105\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( x \\), add 137 to both sides of the equation:\n     \\[\n     x - 137 + 137 = 105 + 137\n     \\]\n   - Simplifying the equation gives:\n     \\[\n     x = 242\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Paul initially had 242 books before selling 137 at the garage sale.\n\nTherefore, Paul had 242 books initially.'

'To solve the problem of distributing 14 cookies equally among 7 bags, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Total number of cookies = 14\n   - Total number of bags = 7\n   - Cookies are distributed equally among the bags.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of cookies in each bag.\n   - Since the cookies are distributed equally, the equation is:\n     \\[\n     7x = 14\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Divide both sides of the equation by 7 to find \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{14}{7}\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the division:\n     \\[\n     x = 2\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each bag contains 2 cookies.\n\nTherefore, each bag has 2 cookies.'
"To solve the problem of how many crackers each of Matthew's 18 friends ate, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Total Number of Crackers:**\n   - Matthew had a total of 36 crackers.\n\n2. **Understand the Number of Friends:**\n   - Matthew distributed the crackers equally among his 18 friends.\n\n3. **Calculate the Number of Crackers per Friend:**\n   - To find out how many crackers each friend received, divide the total number of crackers by the number of friends.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of crackers per friend} = \\frac{\\text{Total number of crackers}}{\\text{Number of friends}} = \\frac{36}{18}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the Division:**\n   - \\(\\frac{36}{18} = 2\\)\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each of Matthew's 18 friends ate 2 crackers.\n\nTherefore, each friend received and ate 2 crackers."

Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the weekly rent payment:**\n   - Lewis pays $388 in rent every week.\n\n2. **Identify the duration of the harvest season:**\n   - The harvest season lasts for 1359 weeks.\n\n3. **Calculate the total rent paid over the harvest season:**\n   - Multiply the weekly rent payment by the number of weeks in the harvest season.\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total Rent} = \\text{Weekly Rent} \\times \\text{Number of Weeks}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total Rent} = 388 \\times 1359\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the multiplication:**\n   - Calculate \\(388 \\times 1359\\).\n\n   Let's do the multiplication:\n   \\[\n   388 \\times 1359 = 527,892\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Lewis pays a total of $527,892 in rent during the 1359 weeks of the harvest season.\n\nTherefore, the total amount of money Lewis pays as rent during the harvest season is $527,892."

'To determine how much money Edward had initially before he spent any of it, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the total amount spent:**\n   - Edward spent $9 initially.\n   - He then spent an additional $8.\n   - Total amount spent = $9 + $8 = $17.\n\n2. **Determine the amount Edward has remaining:**\n   - After spending, Edward has $17 remaining.\n\n3. **Calculate the initial amount Edward had:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the initial amount of money Edward had.\n   - The equation representing the situation is:\n     \\[\n     x - \\text{Total amount spent} = \\text{Amount remaining}\n     \\]\n   - Substitute the known values:\n     \\[\n     x - 17 = 17\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve for \\( x \\):**\n   - Add 17 to both sides of the equation to isolate \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 17 + 17\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the result:\n     \\[\n     x = 34\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, Edward initially had $34 before he spent any of it.'
"To solve the problem, we need to determine how many bird families are left near the mountain after some have migrated to Africa and Asia. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Total bird families living near the mountain initially**: 85\n\n2. **Bird families that flew away to Africa**: 23\n\n3. **Bird families that flew away to Asia**: 37\n\nNow, we need to calculate how many bird families have left in total:\n\n- Total bird families that flew away = Bird families to Africa + Bird families to Asia\n- Total bird families that flew away = 23 + 37 = 60\n\nNext, we subtract the total number of bird families that flew away from the initial number of bird families:\n\n- Bird families left near the mountain = Total initial bird families - Total bird families that flew away\n- Bird families left near the mountain = 85 - 60 = 25\n\nTherefore, 25 bird families were left near the mountain."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Total number of sacks harvested**: 56 sacks\n2. **Duration of the harvest**: 4 days\n\nWe need to find out how many sacks of oranges are harvested per day. To do this, we will divide the total number of sacks by the number of days the harvest lasts.\n\n**Calculation**:\n- Total sacks = 56 sacks\n- Number of days = 4 days\n\nTo find the number of sacks harvested per day, use the formula:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Sacks per day} = \\frac{\\text{Total sacks}}{\\text{Number of days}}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the given values into the formula:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Sacks per day} = \\frac{56 \\text{ sacks}}{4 \\text{ days}} = 14 \\text{ sacks per day}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, they harvest 14 sacks of oranges per day."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial number of roses in the vase**: 21 roses.\n2. **Number of roses thrown away by Jessica**: 34 roses.\n3. **Final number of roses in the vase**: 15 roses.\n\nWe need to find out how many roses Jessica cut from her garden and then determine how many more roses she threw away than she cut.\n\n### Step-by-step Solution:\n\n1. **Calculate the change in the number of roses**:\n   - Jessica started with 21 roses and ended with 15 roses.\n   - The change in the number of roses in the vase is \\( 21 - 15 = 6 \\) roses.\n\n2. **Determine the number of roses cut from the garden**:\n   - Jessica threw away 34 roses, but the net change in the number of roses is only 6 roses fewer than she started with.\n   - This means she must have added some roses to the vase to offset the number she threw away.\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of roses she cut from her garden.\n   - The equation representing the situation is: \n     \\[\n     21 - 34 + x = 15\n     \\]\n   - Simplifying the equation:\n     \\[\n     -13 + x = 15\n     \\]\n   - Solving for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = 15 + 13 = 28\n     \\]\n   - So, Jessica cut 28 roses from her garden.\n\n3. **Calculate how many more roses were thrown away than cut**:\n   - Jessica threw away 34 roses and cut 28 roses.\n   - The difference is:\n     \\[\n     34 - 28 = 6\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, Jessica threw away 6 more roses than she cut from her garden."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Initial Balloons:**\n   - Allan initially brought 2 balloons to the park.\n   - Jake brought 6 balloons to the park.\n\n2. **Additional Balloons:**\n   - Allan bought 3 more balloons at the park.\n\n3. **Total Balloons:**\n   - Allan's total balloons = Initial balloons + Additional balloons\n     \\[\n     2 + 3 = 5\n     \\]\n   - Jake's total balloons = 6 (since he didn't buy any more)\n\n4. **Comparison:**\n   - To find out how many more balloons Jake had than Allan, subtract Allan's total from Jake's total:\n     \\[\n     6 - 5 = 1\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, Jake had 1 more balloon than Allan in the park."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided in the hints:\n\n1. **Daily Harvest:**\n   - Ripe oranges: 28 sacks per day\n   - Unripe oranges: 52 sacks per day\n\n2. **Duration of Harvest:**\n   - 26 days\n\n3. **Calculate Total Sacks of Ripe Oranges:**\n   - Daily ripe sacks = 28\n   - Total ripe sacks over 26 days = 28 sacks/day × 26 days = 728 sacks\n\n4. **Calculate Total Sacks of Unripe Oranges:**\n   - Daily unripe sacks = 52\n   - Total unripe sacks over 26 days = 52 sacks/day × 26 days = 1,352 sacks\n\n5. **Calculate Total Sacks of Oranges:**\n   - Total sacks = Total ripe sacks + Total unripe sacks\n   - Total sacks = 728 sacks + 1,352 sacks = 2,080 sacks\n\nTherefore, after 26 days of harvest, they will have a total of 2,080 sacks of oranges."
"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understanding the Problem:**\n   - Together, Adam and Jackie have 6 apples.\n   - Jackie has 4 more apples than the combined total of Adam and Jackie.\n\n2. **Setting Up the Equations:**\n   - Let \\( A \\) represent the number of apples Adam has.\n   - Let \\( J \\) represent the number of apples Jackie has.\n\n3. **Using the Information:**\n   - From the first piece of information, we have:\n     \\[\n     A + J = 6\n     \\]\n   - From the second piece of information, Jackie has 4 more apples than the combined total of Adam and Jackie:\n     \\[\n     J = (A + J) + 4\n     \\]\n\n4. **Substituting the First Equation into the Second:**\n   - Substitute \\( A + J = 6 \\) into the second equation:\n     \\[\n     J = 6 + 4\n     \\]\n   - Simplify:\n     \\[\n     J = 10\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Jackie has 10 apples.\n\nTherefore, Jackie has 10 apples."
"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and perform the calculations:\n\n1. **Initial Number of Trees:**\n   - Haley initially had 11 trees.\n\n2. **Trees that Died:**\n   - After the typhoon, 2 trees died.\n\n3. **Calculate the Number of Trees that Survived:**\n   - Subtract the number of trees that died from the initial number of trees to find out how many survived:\n   \\[\n   11 - 2 = 9\n   \\]\n   - So, 9 trees survived the typhoon.\n\n4. **Calculate the Difference Between Survived and Died Trees:**\n   - Subtract the number of trees that died from the number of trees that survived to find out how many more trees survived than died:\n   \\[\n   9 - 2 = 7\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, 7 more trees survived the typhoon than those that died."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - David did 37 push-ups.\n   - David did 30 more push-ups than Zachary.\n\n2. **Define the Relationship:**\n   - Let \\( Z \\) represent the number of push-ups Zachary did.\n   - According to the problem, David did 30 more push-ups than Zachary. This can be expressed as:\n     \\[\n     \\text{David's push-ups} = Z + 30\n     \\]\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - We know from the problem that David did 37 push-ups. So, we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     Z + 30 = 37\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve for \\( Z \\):**\n   - Subtract 30 from both sides of the equation to solve for \\( Z \\):\n     \\[\n     Z + 30 - 30 = 37 - 30\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     Z = 7\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Zachary did 7 push-ups.\n\nTherefore, Zachary did 7 push-ups."

"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and question information:\n\n1. **Understand the given information:**\n   - The length of Jesse's room is 7 feet.\n   - The area of the carpet needed is 14 square feet.\n\n2. **Identify what needs to be found:**\n   - We need to find the width of Jesse's room.\n\n3. **Use the formula for the area of a rectangle:**\n   - The area of a rectangle is given by the formula: \n     \\[\n     \\text{Area} = \\text{Length} \\times \\text{Width}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Substitute the known values into the formula:**\n   - We know the area is 14 square feet and the length is 7 feet. So, we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     14 = 7 \\times \\text{Width}\n     \\]\n\n5. **Solve for the width:**\n   - To find the width, divide both sides of the equation by 7:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Width} = \\frac{14}{7} = 2\n     \\]\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - The width of Jesse's room is 2 feet.\n\nTherefore, the width of Jesse's room is 2 feet."

"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and question:\n\n1. **Understand the rate of production:**\n   - The industrial machine can make 6 shirts per minute.\n\n2. **Determine the time the machine worked today:**\n   - The machine worked for 12 minutes today.\n\n3. **Calculate the total number of shirts made today:**\n   - Use the formula: \n     \\[\n     \\text{Total shirts made} = \\text{Shirts per minute} \\times \\text{Minutes worked}\n     \\]\n   - Substitute the given values:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total shirts made} = 6 \\, \\text{shirts/minute} \\times 12 \\, \\text{minutes}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Perform the calculation:**\n   - \\[\n     6 \\times 12 = 72\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The industrial machine made 72 shirts today.\n\nTherefore, the machine made 72 shirts today."

"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Identify the number of girls:**\n   - There are 868 girls in the school.\n\n2. **Understand the relationship between the number of girls and boys:**\n   - There are 281 more girls than boys.\n\n3. **Set up an equation to find the number of boys:**\n   - Let \\( B \\) represent the number of boys.\n   - According to the problem, the number of girls is 281 more than the number of boys. Therefore, we can write the equation:\n     \\[\n     868 = B + 281\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the equation for \\( B \\):**\n   - Subtract 281 from both sides to find the number of boys:\n     \\[\n     B = 868 - 281\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the result:\n     \\[\n     B = 587\n     \\]\n\n5. **Calculate the total number of pupils:**\n   - The total number of pupils is the sum of the number of girls and boys:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total pupils} = 868 + 587\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the result:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total pupils} = 1455\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, there are 1,455 pupils in the school."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - David did 51 push-ups.\n   - David did 49 more push-ups than Zachary.\n\n2. **Determine How Many Push-ups Zachary Did:**\n   - Since David did 49 more push-ups than Zachary, we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     \\text{David's push-ups} = \\text{Zachary's push-ups} + 49\n     \\]\n   - We know David did 51 push-ups, so:\n     \\[\n     51 = \\text{Zachary's push-ups} + 49\n     \\]\n   - To find out how many push-ups Zachary did, subtract 49 from 51:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Zachary's push-ups} = 51 - 49 = 2\n     \\]\n\n3. **Calculate the Total Number of Push-ups Done by Both:**\n   - Add the number of push-ups done by David and Zachary:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total push-ups} = \\text{David's push-ups} + \\text{Zachary's push-ups} = 51 + 2\n     \\]\n   - Therefore, the total number of push-ups done by both is:\n     \\[\n     51 + 2 = 53\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Zachary and David did a total of 53 push-ups altogether.\n\nSo, the answer is 53 push-ups."

"To solve the problem, we need to determine the total number of visitors to Buckingham Palace over the past 89 days, given the number of visitors for the current day and the two preceding days. Here's a step-by-step breakdown:\n\n1. **Current Day Visitors**: 512 visitors\n2. **Previous Day Visitors**: 471 visitors\n3. **Two Days Before Current Day Visitors**: 808 visitors\n\nWe need to find the total number of visitors over the past 89 days. However, we only have data for the last three days. To proceed, we need to make an assumption or find a pattern for the remaining 86 days. Since the problem doesn't provide specific data for these days, we can assume an average or use the given data to estimate.\n\nLet's assume the average number of visitors per day over the past 89 days is the average of the three given days. This is a common approach when specific data is not available.\n\n4. **Calculate the Average Number of Visitors for the Three Days**:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Average visitors per day} = \\frac{512 + 471 + 808}{3} = \\frac{1791}{3} = 597\n   \\]\n\n5. **Estimate Total Visitors for 89 Days**:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total visitors for 89 days} = 597 \\times 89 = 53,133\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, based on the assumption that the average number of visitors per day is consistent with the average of the three given days, approximately 53,133 visitors came to Buckingham Palace within the past 89 days."

"To solve the problem, we need to determine how many weeks Lewis worked during the harvest to earn a total of $1216, given that he earns $16 each week. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the total earnings during the harvest:**\n   - Total earnings = $1216\n\n2. **Identify the earnings per week:**\n   - Earnings per week = $16\n\n3. **Set up the equation to find the number of weeks:**\n   - Let \\( w \\) represent the number of weeks.\n   - The equation based on the information given is:\n     \\[\n     16w = 1216\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve for \\( w \\):**\n   - Divide both sides of the equation by 16 to isolate \\( w \\):\n     \\[\n     w = \\frac{1216}{16}\n     \\]\n\n5. **Perform the division:**\n   - Calculate \\( \\frac{1216}{16} \\):\n     \\[\n     w = 76\n     \\]\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - The harvest lasted for 76 weeks.\n\nTherefore, Lewis worked for 76 weeks during the harvest."

"To solve the problem, we need to determine how much money the ring toss game made per day over the 5 days. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Total Earnings:**\n   - The ring toss game earned a total of $165 over 5 days.\n\n2. **Understand the Daily Earnings:**\n   - The game made the same amount of money each day.\n\n3. **Set Up the Calculation:**\n   - To find out how much was made per day, we need to divide the total earnings by the number of days.\n\n4. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Total earnings = $165\n   - Number of days = 5\n   - Daily earnings = Total earnings ÷ Number of days\n   - Daily earnings = $165 ÷ 5\n\n5. **Calculate:**\n   - $165 ÷ 5 = $33\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   - The ring toss game made $33 per day.\n\nTherefore, the ring toss game made $33 each day."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Initial Count:**\n   - There were initially 5 roses in the vase.\n   - There were initially 3 orchids in the vase.\n\n2. **Current Count:**\n   - There are now 12 roses in the vase.\n   - There are now 2 orchids in the vase.\n\n3. **Calculate the Difference:**\n   - To find out how many more roses than orchids are in the vase now, subtract the number of orchids from the number of roses.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Difference} = \\text{Number of Roses} - \\text{Number of Orchids} = 12 - 2 = 10\n   \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - There are 10 more roses than orchids in the vase now.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that there are 10 more roses than orchids in the vase."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Each seat on the Ferris wheel can hold 9 people.\n   - A total of 18 people can ride the Ferris wheel at the same time.\n\n2. **Determine the Number of Seats:**\n   - We need to find out how many seats are required to accommodate 18 people if each seat can hold 9 people.\n\n3. **Calculation:**\n   - To find the number of seats, divide the total number of people by the number of people each seat can hold.\n   - Calculation: \\( \\frac{18 \\text{ people}}{9 \\text{ people per seat}} = 2 \\text{ seats} \\)\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - The Ferris wheel has 2 seats.\n\nTherefore, the Ferris wheel has 2 seats."
'To solve the problem of determining how many apps Dave initially had on his phone, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Dave deleted 18 apps from his phone.\n   - After deleting, he had 5 apps left.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) represent the initial number of apps Dave had on his phone.\n   - According to the problem, after deleting 18 apps, Dave was left with 5 apps. This can be expressed as:\n     \\[\n     x - 18 = 5\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( x \\), add 18 to both sides of the equation:\n     \\[\n     x - 18 + 18 = 5 + 18\n     \\]\n   - Simplifying the equation gives:\n     \\[\n     x = 23\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Dave initially had 23 apps on his phone.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Dave had 23 apps on his phone initially before deleting 18 of them.'

'To find out how much each pack of DVDs costs, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Total Cost for 2 Packs of DVDs**:  \n   The total cost given for 2 packs is 28 dollars.\n\n2. **Number of Packs Purchased**:  \n   The number of packs purchased is 2.\n\n3. **Calculate the Cost per Pack**:  \n   To find the cost of one pack, divide the total cost by the number of packs.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Cost per pack} = \\frac{\\text{Total cost}}{\\text{Number of packs}} = \\frac{28 \\text{ dollars}}{2 \\text{ packs}} = 14 \\text{ dollars per pack}\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, each pack of DVDs costs 14 dollars.'

Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the points per round:**\n   - Luke gained 146 points in each round.\n\n2. **Identify the number of rounds played:**\n   - Luke played 157 rounds.\n\n3. **Calculate the total points:**\n   - Multiply the points per round by the number of rounds:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Total Points} = 146 \\, \\text{points/round} \\times 157 \\, \\text{rounds}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Perform the multiplication:**\n   - First, multiply 146 by 157:\n     \\[\n     146 \\times 157 = 22922\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Luke scored a total of 22,922 points in the game.\n\nTherefore, the total points Luke scored in the game is 22,922."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Information:**\n   - Initially, there were some roses in the vase. Let's call this initial number of roses \\( x \\).\n   - Jessica cut 16 more roses from her flower garden and added them to the vase.\n   - After adding these 16 roses, there are now 23 roses in the vase.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - The initial number of roses in the vase is \\( x \\).\n   - Jessica added 16 roses, so the total number of roses in the vase becomes \\( x + 16 \\).\n   - We know that after adding the roses, the total is 23 roses.\n\n3. **Formulate the Equation:**\n   \\[\n   x + 16 = 23\n   \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Subtract 16 from both sides to find the initial number of roses:\n   \\[\n   x = 23 - 16\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x = 7\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - There were initially 7 roses in the vase before Jessica added the 16 more roses.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that there were 7 roses in the vase at the beginning."

Based on the calculations:\n\n- **The frog jumped 58 inches.**"

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Information Given:**\n   - On the day Rachel visited, 132 visitors came to Buckingham Palace.\n   - A total of 406 people visited Buckingham Palace over the past 327 days.\n\n2. **Objective:**\n   - Find out how many visitors visited Buckingham Palace on the day before Rachel's visit.\n\n3. **Calculation Steps:**\n   - First, we need to determine the total number of visitors for the 326 days before Rachel's visit (since the 327th day is the day of her visit).\n   - We know that the total number of visitors over 327 days is 406.\n   - On the day of Rachel's visit, there were 132 visitors.\n\n4. **Calculate the Total Visitors for the Previous 326 Days:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total visitors for 326 days} = \\text{Total visitors for 327 days} - \\text{Visitors on Rachel's visit day}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total visitors for 326 days} = 406 - 132 = 274\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The total number of visitors for the 326 days before Rachel's visit is 274.\n   - Since we need to find the number of visitors on the day before Rachel's visit, we assume that the 326 days include the day before her visit.\n   - Therefore, the number of visitors on the day before Rachel's visit is the total number of visitors for the 326 days.\n\nThus, the number of visitors who visited Buckingham Palace on the day before Rachel's visit is 274."

'To solve the problem of determining how many cookies Paco had initially, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Information Given:**\n   - Paco ate 19 cookies.\n   - After eating, he had 35 cookies left.\n\n2. **Define the Problem:**\n   - We need to find out how many cookies Paco had initially before he ate any.\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the number of cookies Paco had initially.\n   - After eating 19 cookies, he had 35 cookies left.\n   - Therefore, the equation is: \n     \\[\n     x - 19 = 35\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve the Equation:**\n   - Add 19 to both sides of the equation to solve for \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x - 19 + 19 = 35 + 19\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     x = 54\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Paco initially had 54 cookies.\n\nTherefore, the answer is that Paco had 54 cookies in the beginning.'
'To solve the problem of determining how many bags of cookies you have, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Each bag contains 3 cookies.\n   - You have a total of 21 cookies.\n\n2. **Set Up the Calculation:**\n   - You need to find out how many bags are needed to hold 21 cookies if each bag holds 3 cookies.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   - Divide the total number of cookies by the number of cookies per bag:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Number of bags} = \\frac{\\text{Total cookies}}{\\text{Cookies per bag}} = \\frac{21}{3}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Calculate:**\n   - \\(\\frac{21}{3} = 7\\)\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - You have 7 bags of cookies.\n\nTherefore, you have 7 bags of cookies.'

'To solve the problem of determining how many drums of grapes are filled per day by 94 pickers, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the given information:**\n   - Number of pickers: 94\n   - Total number of drums filled: 90\n   - Total number of days: 6\n\n2. **Identify the core question:**\n   - How many drums of grapes are filled per day?\n\n3. **Calculate the number of drums filled per day:**\n   - We know that 90 drums are filled in 6 days.\n   - To find out how many drums are filled per day, we divide the total number of drums by the total number of days.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Drums filled per day} = \\frac{\\text{Total number of drums}}{\\text{Total number of days}} = \\frac{90}{6} = 15\n   \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Therefore, 15 drums of grapes are filled per day by the 94 pickers.\n\nThe answer is that 15 drums of grapes are filled per day.'

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Total visitors in the past 85 days**: 829\n2. **Visitors on the previous day**: 45\n\nWe need to find out how many visitors visited the Buckingham Palace on the day they went.\n\n**Step 1**: Calculate the total number of visitors for the 84 days before the day they went.\n\nSince the total number of visitors over the past 85 days is 829, and 45 of those visitors came on the previous day, we can find the number of visitors for the 84 days before the day they went by subtracting the visitors from the previous day:\n\n\\[ 829 - 45 = 784 \\]\n\nSo, 784 visitors came in the 84 days before the day they went.\n\n**Step 2**: Calculate the number of visitors on the day they went.\n\nNow, we know that the total number of visitors over the 85 days is 829. We have already accounted for 784 visitors in the 84 days before the day they went and 45 visitors on the previous day. Therefore, the number of visitors on the day they went is:\n\n\\[ 829 - 784 = 45 \\]\n\nThus, 45 visitors visited the Buckingham Palace on the day they went."

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the total number of baskets:**\n   - There are 2 baskets.\n\n2. **Determine the number of red peaches in each basket:**\n   - Each basket contains 4 red peaches.\n\n3. **Calculate the total number of red peaches in both baskets:**\n   - Since there are 2 baskets and each has 4 red peaches, the total number of red peaches is:\n     \\[\n     2 \\times 4 = 8 \\text{ red peaches}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Identify the total number of peaches in both baskets:**\n   - There are a total of 12 peaches in both baskets combined.\n\n5. **Calculate the total number of green peaches in both baskets:**\n   - Subtract the total number of red peaches from the total number of peaches to find the total number of green peaches:\n     \\[\n     12 - 8 = 4 \\text{ green peaches}\n     \\]\n\n6. **Determine the number of green peaches in each basket:**\n   - Since the 4 green peaches are distributed equally between the 2 baskets, each basket contains:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{4}{2} = 2 \\text{ green peaches per basket}\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, each basket contains 2 green peaches."

Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Each block receives 38 pieces of junk mail.\n   - There are 19 houses on each block.\n   - We need to find out how many pieces of junk mail each house should receive.\n\n2. **Calculate the Number of Pieces of Junk Mail per House:**\n   - Since each block receives 38 pieces of junk mail and there are 19 houses on each block, we need to divide the total number of pieces of junk mail per block by the number of houses on that block.\n\n3. **Perform the Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Pieces of junk mail per house} = \\frac{\\text{Total pieces of junk mail per block}}{\\text{Number of houses per block}} = \\frac{38}{19}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the Result:**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{38}{19} = 2\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - Each house should receive 2 pieces of junk mail.\n\nTherefore, the mailman should give each house 2 pieces of junk mail."

"To find the width of Jesse's room, we can use the formula for the area of a rectangle, which is:\n\n\\[ \\text{Area} = \\text{Length} \\times \\text{Width} \\]\n\nGiven:\n- The area of the room (carpet size needed) is 10 square feet.\n- The length of the room is 5 feet.\n\nWe need to find the width of the room. Let's solve the problem step by step:\n\n1. **Write down the formula for the area of a rectangle:**\n\n   \\[ \\text{Area} = \\text{Length} \\times \\text{Width} \\]\n\n2. **Substitute the known values into the formula:**\n\n   \\[ 10 = 5 \\times \\text{Width} \\]\n\n3. **Solve for the width:**\n\n   \\[ \\text{Width} = \\frac{10}{5} \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the width:**\n\n   \\[ \\text{Width} = 2 \\]\n\nTherefore, the width of Jesse's room is 2 feet."

Let's go through the steps:\n\n1. **Determine the total number of Skittles and erasers:**\n   - Total Skittles = 4502\n   - Total erasers = 4276\n\n2. **Calculate the combined total of Skittles and erasers:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total items} = \\text{Total Skittles} + \\text{Total erasers} = 4502 + 4276\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total items} = 8778\n   \\]\n\n3. **Determine the number of groups:**\n   - Total groups = 154\n\n4. **Calculate the size of each group:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Size of each group} = \\frac{\\text{Total items}}{\\text{Total groups}} = \\frac{8778}{154}\n   \\]\n\n5. **Perform the division:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Size of each group} = 57\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, each group contains 57 items."
"To solve this problem, we need to calculate the total number of pieces of junk mail the mailman has to deliver. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Determine the number of pieces of junk mail per house:**\n   - Each house receives 4 pieces of junk mail.\n\n2. **Calculate the total number of houses:**\n   - There are 17 houses in each block.\n   - There are 16 blocks in total.\n   - Total number of houses = 17 houses/block × 16 blocks = 272 houses.\n\n3. **Calculate the total number of pieces of junk mail:**\n   - Since each house receives 4 pieces of junk mail, the total number of pieces of junk mail is:\n   - Total pieces of junk mail = 4 pieces/house × 272 houses = 1,088 pieces.\n\nTherefore, the mailman needs to deliver a total of 1,088 pieces of junk mail."

"To solve the problem, we need to determine how many points Luke scored per round, given that he scored a total of 84 points over 2 rounds, with the same number of points gained in each round. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Total Points Scored**: Luke scored a total of 84 points.\n\n2. **Number of Rounds Played**: Luke played 2 rounds.\n\n3. **Points Per Round**: We need to find out how many points Luke scored in each round, knowing that the points per round are the same.\n\nTo find the points scored per round, we can use the formula:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Points per round} = \\frac{\\text{Total points scored}}{\\text{Number of rounds played}}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the given values into the formula:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Points per round} = \\frac{84}{2} = 42\n\\]\n\nTherefore, Luke scored 42 points per round."

'To solve this problem, let\'s break down the information given and address any inconsistencies:\n\n1. **Total Seeds Planted**: Paige and her mom planted a total of 55 seeds.\n\n2. **Seeds per Flower Bed**: They put 15 seeds in each flower bed.\n\n3. **Inconsistency**: The statement that "60 seeds grew into flowers in each flower bed" is inconsistent because they only planted 55 seeds in total. Therefore, it\'s impossible for 60 seeds to grow in each flower bed.\n\nGiven these points, let\'s proceed with the logical steps:\n\n### Step-by-Step Solution:\n\n1. **Determine the Number of Flower Beds**:\n   - Since they planted 15 seeds in each flower bed, we can calculate the number of flower beds by dividing the total seeds by the seeds per bed:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of flower beds} = \\frac{55 \\text{ seeds}}{15 \\text{ seeds/bed}} \\approx 3.67\n   \\]\n   Since you can\'t have a fraction of a flower bed, this suggests they used 3 full flower beds and had some seeds left over.\n\n2. **Calculate Seeds in Each Bed**:\n   - For 3 flower beds, they would have used:\n   \\[\n   3 \\text{ beds} \\times 15 \\text{ seeds/bed} = 45 \\text{ seeds}\n   \\]\n   - This leaves:\n   \\[\n   55 \\text{ total seeds} - 45 \\text{ seeds used} = 10 \\text{ seeds left over}\n   \\]\n   - These 10 leftover seeds could be planted in a partial or additional bed.\n\n3. **Determine How Many Seeds Grew**:\n   - Since the information about 60 seeds growing per bed is incorrect, we need to assume a reasonable growth rate. Without specific growth data, let\'s assume all planted seeds grew into flowers (a common assumption in such problems unless stated otherwise).\n\n4. **Total Flowers Grown**:\n   - If all 55 seeds grew into flowers, then the total number of flowers is 55.\n\n### Conclusion:\nThe total number of flowers that grew from the seeds Paige and her mom planted is 55.'

"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided:\n\n1. **Information Given:**\n   - The grasshopper jumped 13 inches.\n   - The grasshopper jumped 2 inches farther than the frog.\n\n2. **Understanding the Relationship:**\n   - If the grasshopper jumped 2 inches farther than the frog, then the frog's jump distance is 2 inches less than the grasshopper's jump.\n\n3. **Setting Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( F \\) represent the distance the frog jumped.\n   - According to the information, the grasshopper's jump (13 inches) is 2 inches more than the frog's jump. Therefore, we can write the equation:\n     \\[\n     13 = F + 2\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solving the Equation:**\n   - To find \\( F \\), subtract 2 from both sides of the equation:\n     \\[\n     F = 13 - 2\n     \\]\n   - Calculate the result:\n     \\[\n     F = 11\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The frog jumped 11 inches.\n\nTherefore, the frog jumped 11 inches."
